Refuting Existence and Qualification as the Dependent
Sanusi refutes the second and third divisions of the dependent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why neither existence nor the qualification of quiddity by existence can be the thing that depends on an efficient cause, and how these refutations rely on the same logic used against quiddity.

Core Idea
Existence and qualification are not real dependents—they collapse into quiddity or regress.

The author has already refuted the idea that quiddity itself is the dependent. Now he tackles two other possibilities: that existence is dependent, or that the qualification of quiddity by existence is dependent. Both are shown to be impossible through the same arguments already established. This passage tightens the case that nothing in the chain of dependence can escape pointing back to a self-sufficient creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic source alongside the literal translation to get the flow of the argument. Notice how the author structures the refutation in two main divisions, each with its own reasoning.
Pay attention to the technical terms: الوجود, موصوفية, التسلسل.
2
Identify the three possibilities being refuted
The passage refers back to a previous division. The first possibility (quiddity) was already refuted. Here, the second is existence, and the third is the qualification of quiddity by existence. Identify each and see how the refutations differ.
3
Understand the refutation of the second division
The author argues that existence itself is a quiddity, so the same arguments that refuted quiddity also refute existence. Make sure you see why existence can't be a dependent without leading to regress.
4
Understand the two refutations of the third division
The third division is refuted from two angles: first, the qualification is not a real additional attribute, so it cannot be an effect. Second, even if it were an attribute, it would lead to regress or circularity. Walk through each argument step by step.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
After studying both refutations, consider how they collectively show that every candidate for the dependent (quiddity, existence, qualification) fails. This reinforces the doctrine that only the Necessary Being is independent.
This is a key step in establishing tawhid in the context of causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال المحتاج إلى المؤثر والجاعل يمتنع أن يكون هو الوجود. فهذا أيضاً باطل لأن الوجود من حيث إنه وجود: ماهية من الماهيات، وحقيقة من الحقائق، والدليلان المذكوران في امتناع كون الماهية مجعولة يجريان بعينهما في امتناع كون الوجود مجعولاً. وأما القسم الثالث: وهو أن يقال المحتاج إلى الفاعل، والجاعل والمؤثر هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود فنقول: هذا أيضاً باطل من وجهين: الأول: إن موصوفية الماهية بالوجود ليس أمراً زائداً على الماهية وعلى الوجود، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع الحكم عليها بكونها مجعولة. بيان الأول: إنه لو كانت موصوفية الماهية بالوجود أمراً زائداً مغايراً لهما، لكانت موصوفية الماهية بتلك الموصوفية مغايرة، ولزم التسلسل. وبيان الثاني: إن هذه الموصوفية لما لم تكن أمراً ثبوتياً مغايراً، فإنه يمتنع القول بكونها أثراً للفاعل والجاعل، وذلك باطل، لأن ما لا ثبوت له في نفسه، كيف يعقل جعله أثراً للمؤثر والفاعل؟ الوجه الثاني: في إبطال قوله: الواقع بالفاعل هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود، أن نقول: هذه الموصوفية إما أن تكون أمراً وجودياً، وإما أن لا تكون، فإن كان أمراً وجودياً فحينئذ يكون له ماهية، ويكون له وجود، وحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور فيه من أن الواقع بالفاعل، إما ماهيته أو وجوده، فيكون التسلسل أو الدور.
As for the second division: that it is said the one in need of the effect and agent cannot be existence. This too is false, because existence as existence is a quiddity among quiddities and a reality among realities, and the two proofs mentioned concerning the impossibility of the quiddity being made run identically in the impossibility of existence being made. As for the third division: that it is said the one in need of the agent, maker, and effect is the qualification of quiddity by existence. We say: This too is false from two aspects. The first: The qualification of quiddity by existence is not an additional thing over the quiddity and over existence; and if so, it is impossible to judge it as being made. Clarification of the first: If the qualification of quiddity by existence were an additional thing different from them, then the qualification of quiddity by that qualification would be different, and infinite regress would follow. And clarification of the second: Since this qualification is not a positive (thubuti) thing different, it is impossible to say it is an effect of the agent and maker, and that is false, because whatever has no subsistence in itself, how can it be intelligible to make it an effect of the effect and agent? The second aspect: In refuting his statement: 'What is realized by the agent is the qualification of quiddity by existence,' we say: This qualification either is an existential thing or not. If it is an existential thing, then it has a quiddity and has existence, and then the aforementioned division returns into it: that what is realized by the agent is either its quiddity or its existence, so there would be regress or circularity.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the fifth doubt, now addressing the second and third divisions. The second division claims that existence (wujud) itself is the dependent. The author dismisses this: existence as such is a quiddity and reality, so the same proofs against quiddity apply—existence cannot be 'made' because it is a quiddity. The third division claims that the dependent is the qualification of quiddity by existence (mawsufiyyah). The author gives two refutations. First, this qualification is not a real, additional thing; it is merely a relation. If it were additional, infinite regress would arise. Since it is not a fixed (thubuti) entity, it cannot be an effect. Second, even if one insists it is a real attribute, then it itself would have a quiddity and existence, leading to the same division and hence regress or circularity. Thus all three possibilities are impossible, so the original doubt fails.

Key Terms
الوجود
موصوفية الماهية بالوجود
التسلسل
الدور
الأمر الثبوتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The qualification of quiddity by existence (mawsufiyyah) is a real attribute that can be caused independently.
Correction: The author argues it is not an additional real thing; it is merely a relation or an aspect that has no independent subsistence, so it cannot be an effect.

Checkpoint
What does the first proof of the third division argue about the qualification of quiddity by existence?
A) It is a real attribute that can be made.
B) It is not an additional thing over quiddity and existence.
C) It is identical to existence.
D) It is the same as quiddity.

Key Takeaway
Neither existence nor the qualification of quiddity by existence can be the dependent—they either reduce to quiddity or lead to regress, so only the Necessary Being is truly independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, what do you unconsciously rely upon as if it were the ultimate cause of your security or success? How does this lesson's argument that only the Necessary Being is truly independent shake that assumption? Will you actively remind yourself of this when you feel anxious about created means?
?
Consider a time you attributed a result to a secondary cause without acknowledging Allah as the true agent. How does the refutation of 'qualification of quiddity by existence' expose the error of seeing cause and effect as independent? What specific step will you take this week to train your heart to see Allah behind every apparent cause?
?
The lesson shows that even 'existence' itself cannot be the dependent—it is a quiddity. What does this imply about your own existence? Are you living as if your existence is self-sufficient or a gift continuously sustained? If you truly believed you had no independent subsistence, how would your attitude toward Allah's commands change today?

Refutation of the Third Division: Qualification of Essence by Existence
Sanusi refutes the third division with two aspects: non-addition and existence dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the qualification of the essence by existence cannot be the effect of the agent, according to two distinct arguments.

Core Idea
The qualification is either not an extra thing or leads to regress—either way it cannot be an effect.

The third division proposes that what is in need of an agent is the very qualification of the essence by existence. Sanusi refutes this with two independent arguments: first, this qualification is not an additional positive reality, and second, if it were, it would lead to an infinite regress or reintroduce the original problem. These arguments show that the qualification cannot serve as the effect of the agent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage for the third division refutation. Then read the translation. Notice the two main aspects (الوجه الأول and الوجه الثاني).
The passage begins with 'وأما القسم الثالث' and ends just before 'وأما القسم الرابع'.
2
Identify the two aspects of the argument
The first aspect argues that the qualification is not an additional thing; the second poses a dilemma about its existence. Under each, find the sub-arguments.
The first aspect has two explanations: one about infinite regress, the other about lacking positive status.
3
Understand why each aspect disproves the claim
Consider how each argument shows that the qualification cannot be a genuine effect. Ask yourself: what must be true for something to be an effect?
The key is that an effect must be a positive, distinct thing—but the qualification fails this test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث : وهو أن يقال المحتاج إلى الفاعل ، والجاعل والمؤثر هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود فنقول : هذا أيضاً باطل من وجهين : الأول : إن موصوفية الماهية بالوجود ليس أمراً زائداً على الماهية وعلى الوجود، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع الحكم عليها بكونها مجعولة . بيان الأول : إنه لو كانت موصوفية الماهية بالوجود أمراً زائداً مغايراً لهما، لكانت موصوفية الماهية بتلك الموصوفية مغايرة، ولزم التسلسل . وبيان الثاني : إن هذه الموصوفية لما لم تكن أمراً ثبوتياً مغايراً ، فإنه يمتنع القول بكونها أثراً للفاعل والجاعل ، وذلك باطل، لأن ما لا ثبوت له في نفسه، كيف يعقل جعله أثراً للمؤثر والفاعل ؟ الوجه الثاني : في إبطال قوله : الواقع بالفاعل هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود، أن نقول : هذه الموصوفية إما أن تكون أمراً وجودياً ، وإما أن لا تكون ، فإن كان أمراً وجودياً فحينئذ يكون له ماهية، ويكون له وجود، وحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور فيه من أن الواقع بالفاعل، إما ماهيته أو وجوده، وإن لم يكن له وجود البتة، استحال القول بأن الواقع بالفاعل والجاعل هو هو، فثبت بما ذكرنا : أنه يمتنع القول بأن تأثير الفاعل في الماهية ممتنع، ويمتنع القول بأن تأثيره في الوجود، ويمتنع القول بأن تأثيره في موصوفية الماهية بالوجود . وأما القسم الرابع وهو بيان أنه لما ظهر بطلان الأقسام كان القول بالتأثير والمؤثر باطلا، فتقريره : أن ذلك الأثر لما كان غنيا في ماهيته عن المؤثر، وكان غنياً في وجوده عن المؤثر، وكان غنياً في اتصاف ماهيته بوجوده عن المؤثر، كانت هذه الماهية الموجودة غنية عن المؤثر والفاعل . لأنه متى حصلت الماهية، وحصل الوجود، وحصلت موصوفية الماهية بالوجود، فقد حصلت الماهية الموجودة بدون هذا المؤثر، وهذا الفاعل . وإذا كان كذلك كانت هذه الماهية الموجودة غنية عن المؤثر. وذلك هو المطلوب
As for the third division: that it is said the thing in need of the agent, the maker, and the effecter is the qualification of the essence by existence. So we say: this too is false from two aspects. The first: that the qualification of the essence by existence is not an additional thing beyond the essence and beyond existence, and if it is so, it is impossible to judge it as being made. Explanation of the first: if the qualification of the essence by existence were an additional thing different from them, then the qualification of the essence by that qualification would be different, and an infinite regress would follow. And explanation of the second: since this qualification is not a positive thing different, it is impossible to say that it is an effect of the agent and maker, and that is false, because something that has no positive existence in itself, how can it be understood to be made an effect of the effecter and agent? The second aspect: in refuting his statement: 'what is brought about by the agent is the qualification of the essence by existence', is that we say: this qualification is either an existent thing or not. If it is an existent thing, then it has an essence and it has existence, and then the mentioned division returns regarding it as to whether what is brought about by the agent is its essence or its existence. And if it has no existence at all, it is impossible to say that what is brought about by the agent and maker is it. So it is established by what we have mentioned: that it is impossible to say that the agent's effect in the essence is impossible, and it is impossible to say that his effect is in existence, and it is impossible to say that his effect is in the qualification of the essence by existence. As for the fourth division: it is an exposition that when the falsity of the divisions became apparent, then the statement of effect and effecter is false. Its exposition: that since that effect was independent in its essence from the effecter, and independent in its existence from the effecter, and independent in the being of its essence qualified by its existence from the effecter, then this existing essence is independent from the effecter and agent. Because whenever the essence occurs, and existence occurs, and the qualification of the essence by existence occurs, then the existing essence has occurred without this effecter and this agent. And if it is so, then this existing essence is independent of the effecter. And that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a structured refutation of two divisions concerning what is in need of an efficient cause (al-fāʿil). The author first addresses the third division: the claim that what is in need is the qualification (mawṣūfiyya) of the essence (al-māhiyya) by existence (al-wujūd). He argues it is false from two aspects. First, this qualification is not an additional thing over and above essence and existence; if it were additional, it would itself require qualification by another qualification, leading to infinite regress (al-tasalsul). If it is not a positive (thubūtī) distinct thing, it cannot be an effect because something with no positive reality cannot be made. Second, the qualification is either existent or non-existent. If existent, it has its own essence and existence, and the same division applies: is the effect its essence or its existence? If non-existent, it cannot be the effect at all. So all three possibilities for the effect (essence, existence, qualification) are refuted. Then the fourth division concludes that since the effect is independent in its essence, existence, and the combination from the effecter, the existing essence can occur without any effecter, thus the claim of dependency is false.

Key Terms
ماهية (essence)
وجود (existence)
موصوفية (qualification)
أثر (effect)
فاعل (agent)
تسلسل (infinite regress)
ثبوتي (positive)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People may think that the qualification of essence by existence is a distinct attribute that can be caused by an agent.
Correction: The passage shows that this qualification is either not an additional thing (so cannot be an effect) or, if it were additional, it leads to regress or the same problem recurs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the qualification of the essence by existence not a valid candidate for being the effect of the agent?
A) Because it is purely mental and has no reality.
B) Because it is either not an extra thing or, if it is, it leads to the same division and regress.
C) Because it is identical to the essence itself.
D) Because existence is eternal and cannot be effected.

Key Takeaway
The qualification of essence by existence cannot be the agent's effect because it is either not a distinct positive reality or, if it is, the same problem recurs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you ever ponder that it is not a separate 'thing' added to you, but rather that you were nothing and then brought into being by Allah? How does this realization affect your humility before Him?
?
If the qualification of your essence by existence is not an additional reality, then your very being is a direct gift from Allah without any intermediary 'creation' separate from Him. Does this make you feel more dependent on Him? How should this change your daily reliance on Him?
?
Sanusi argues that something with no positive existence cannot be an effect. Your own nonexistence before birth was not a thing that could be acted upon. Yet you are now existent by Allah's will. Does this truth awaken in you a gratitude that acknowledges His absolute power over your being? What will you do today to remind yourself of this?

The Fourth Division: Concluding the Falsity of All Divisions
Sanusi concludes that the effect is independent in essence, existence, and qualification, thus no effecter needed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the falsity of all divisions leads to the conclusion that the effect is independent of the agent.

Core Idea
If the effect is independent in essence, existence, and combination, then no agent is needed.

Having refuted the three possible candidates for the effect (essence, existence, qualification), Sanusi now concludes that the existing essence as a whole is independent of any effecter. The fourth division argues that since each component is independent, the composite is also independent, implying that an agent is not required for the existence of the effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth division passage
Read the Arabic passage for the fourth division and its translation. Notice how it summarizes the refutation of the previous divisions.
The passage begins with 'وأما القسم الرابع' and ends with 'وذلك هو المطلوب'.
2
Identify the three independencies
The passage states that the effect is independent in its essence, in its existence, and in the qualification of its essence by existence. Underline each claim.
These three correspond to the three divisions refuted earlier.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Since all parts are independent, the whole existing essence occurs without the agent. Thus the claim of dependency is false.
The conclusion is that the effect is independent of the agent, which is what was to be proved.

7 min
The Sixth Doubt: The Simple Cannot Be in Need
Argues that the thing judged needy cannot be simple, because possibility does not attach to simple essences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that a simple essence cannot be in need, and how possibility relates to simplicity.

Core Idea
Simplicity blocks possibility, and possibility is the sole cause of need.

This lesson presents the sixth doubt raised against the claim that everything other than Allah is in need. The argument uses an exhaustive division: the thing judged needy is either simple or composite. The focus here is on why a simple being cannot be in need, relying on the nature of possibility.

Guided Path
1
Understand the exhaustive division
Recognize that the thing judged to be in need must be either simple (basīṭ) or composite (murakkab). The author will show both are impossible.
This division sets up the structure of the argument.
2
Grasp the key claim about simples
The author claims that a truly simple essence does not admit possibility (imkān). Why? Because it is impossible to say that a thing can be itself.
Possibility requires a distinction between the subject and the attribute.
3
Examine the example of blackness
The author gives the example: we cannot say 'blackness can be blackness', but we can say 'blackness can remain' or 'can come to be'. The reason is that the concept of blackness is different from the concept of remaining or coming to be.
This illustrates that possibility attaches to states, not to the essence itself.
4
Connect possibility to need
Since the only cause of need is possibility, and possibility does not occur in simples, it follows that need cannot occur in simples.
This completes the refutation for the simple case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السادسة : المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة، إما أن يكون بسيطاً، وإما أن يكون مركباً، والقسمان باطلان، فالقول بالحاجة باطل، أما الحصر فظاهر، وإنما قلنا : إنه ممتنع أن يكون المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة بسيطاً، وذلك لأن البسيط حقاً لا يعرض له الإمكان، لأن من المعلوم بالضرورة أنه يستحيل الحكم على الشيء بأنه يمكن أن يكون هو هو، فيستحيل أن يقال السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً، بل يقال السواد يمكن أن يبقى، ويمكن أن يحدث، إلا أن ذلك إنما يصح لأن المفهوم من السواد مغاير للمفهوم من كونه باقياً وحادثاً، فأما أن يقال : السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً، فهذا غير معقول. فثبت أن الإمكان لا يعرض البتة للحقائق البسيطة، ولما ثبت أنه لا علة للحاجة إلا الإمكان، وثبت أن حصول الإمكان في البائط ممتنع بذلك، ثبت أن حصول الحاجة في البسائط ممتنع . وإنما قلنا : إن
The sixth doubt: the thing judged to be in need and requirement is either simple or composite, and both divisions are false, so the statement of need is false. As for the exhaustive division, it is apparent. And we only say: it is impossible that the thing judged to be in need and requirement be simple, because the truly simple does not admit possibility, because it is known by necessity that it is impossible to judge of a thing that it can be itself. So it is impossible to say 'blackness can be blackness', rather it is said 'blackness can remain' and 'can come to be', except that this is only valid because the concept of blackness is different from the concept of its being remaining and coming to be. As for saying 'blackness can be blackness', this is unintelligible. So it is established that possibility does not at all attach to simple realities. And since it is established that there is no cause for need except possibility, and it is established that the occurrence of possibility in the simple is impossible by that, it is established that the occurrence of need in simples is impossible. And we only say: that
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage introduces the sixth doubt (shubha) against the claim of need. It begins with an exhaustive division: the thing judged to be in need (al-mahkūm ʿalayhi bi-l-iftiqār) is either simple (basīṭ) or composite (murakkab). The author argues both are false. The focus is on the impossibility of a simple being in need. The reason is that the truly simple does not admit possibility (imkān). Necessarily, one cannot say that a thing can be itself; e.g., we cannot say 'blackness can be blackness'. Possibility attaches only to its states, like remaining or coming to be. Since possibility is the sole cause of need, and possibility cannot occur in simples, need cannot occur in simples. The argument cuts off before addressing the composite division.

Key Terms
بسيط (simple)
مركب (composite)
إمكان (possibility)
حاجة (need)
افتقار (dependency)
مفهوم (concept)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a simple essence itself can be described as possible (e.g., 'blackness can be blackness').
Correction: The author clarifies that possibility applies to the states of a thing, not to its essence. A simple is what it is; it cannot be said to be possible or necessary in itself.

Checkpoint
Why is it impossible to say 'blackness can be blackness' according to the passage?
A) Because blackness is a substance.
B) Because possibility attaches to the thing itself, not to its states.
C) Because the concept of blackness is the same as blackness itself, so 'can' is redundant.
D) Because blackness cannot be conceived except as existing.

Key Takeaway
The simple does not admit possibility, and possibility is the sole cause of need, therefore the simple cannot be in need.

Proof that the Existing Essence is Independent of the Agent (Fourth Division)
The author concludes that the existing essence is independent of the agent by refuting three possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author proves that the existing essence is independent of any agent by refuting three possible ways an agent could affect it.

Core Idea
The existing essence needs no agent because it is self-sufficient in essence, existence, and their connection.

This passage concludes a complex argument about causality. The author has considered three ways an agent could act on a thing—on its essence, on its existence, or on the joining of the two—and found all impossible. Now he concludes that the existing essence is independent of any agent. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three refuted possibilities
The passage states that three things are impossible: agent affecting essence, agent affecting existence, and agent affecting the qualification of essence by existence. Understand why each is impossible from the earlier argument (not shown here).
The author assumes these have been proven false earlier.
2
Grasp the conclusion of independence
Since all three possibilities are false, the effect (the existing essence) is independent in its essence, existence, and their connection. Therefore, the entire existing essence is independent of the agent.
3
See the logical summary
The author summarizes: whenever essence, existence, and the qualification of essence by existence are obtained, the existing essence is obtained without the agent. This proves independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يكن له وجود البتة ، استحال القول بأن الواقع بالفاعل والجاعل هو هو ، فثبت بما ذكرنا : أنه يمتنع القول بأن تأثير الفاعل في الماهية ممتنع ، ويمتنع القول بأن تأثيره في الوجود ، ويمتنع القول بأن تأثيره في موصوفية الماهية بالوجود . (1): وأما القسم الرابع وهو بيان أنه لما ظهر بطلان الأقسام كان القول بالتأثير والمؤثر باطلا ، فتقريره : أن ذلك الأثر لما كان غنيا في ماهيته عن المؤثر ، وكان غنياً في وجوده عن المؤثر ، وكان غنياً في اتصاف ماهيته بوجوده عن المؤثر ، كانت هذه الماهية الموجودة غنية عن المؤثر والفاعل . لأنه متى حصلت الماهية ، وحصل الوجود ، وحصلت موصوفية الماهية بالوجود ، فقد حصلت الماهية الموجودة بدون هذا المؤثر ، وهذا الفاعل . وإذا كان كذلك كانت هذه الماهية الموجودة غنية عن المؤثر. وذلك هو المطلوب
And if it has no existence at all, it is impossible to say that what is actual by the agent and maker is it itself. So it is established by what we have mentioned: that it is impossible to say that the agent's effect on the essence is impossible, and it is impossible to say that His effect is on existence, and it is impossible to say that His effect is on the qualification of the essence by existence. (1) As for the fourth division, which is the explanation that when the invalidity of the divisions became apparent, the statement of effect and agent is false. Its exposition: that that effect, since it is independent in its essence from the agent, and is independent in its existence from the agent, and is independent in the qualification of its essence by its existence from the agent, then this existing essence is independent from the agent and the doer. Because whenever the essence is obtained, and existence is obtained, and the qualification of the essence by existence is obtained, then the existing essence has been obtained without this agent and this doer. And if that is the case, then this existing essence is independent of the agent. And that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of the fourth division of an argument refuting the need for an agent. The author begins by stating that if the effect (the thing produced) had no existence at all, it would be impossible to say that what is actual by the agent is the same as the effect. Then he summarizes that it has been proven that three possibilities are false: that the agent's effect is on the essence, that it is on existence, or that it is on the qualification of the essence by existence. Consequently, the division concerning effect and agent is false. He then explains that the effect is independent in its essence, existence, and qualification by existence from the agent. Therefore, the existing essence is obtained without the agent, proving that it is independent. The conclusion is that the existing essence needs no agent.

Key Terms
أثر (effect)
مؤثر (agent)
ماهية (essence)
وجود (existence)
فاعل (doer)
جاعل (maker)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The agent is necessary for the existence of a thing.
Correction: The author argues that the existing essence is independent in essence, existence, and their connection, so it can exist without an agent.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about the existing essence?
A) It is dependent on the agent.
B) It is independent of the agent.
C) It is created by the agent.
D) It is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The existing essence is independent of any agent because it lacks no attribute that an agent could provide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed your identity or worth to something external—a job, a relationship, an achievement—as if that external thing 'gives' you existence? What if your essence and existence are independent, as this passage argues? How would that change your perspective on who you truly are?
?
Consider a time you felt incomplete without an external agent—a person, a possession, a status. The lesson says the existing essence is independent in its essence, existence, and their connection. Does that imply you are already whole? If so, what would it take for you to live from that wholeness right now?
?
If nothing external can truly affect your essence or existence, then what fears lose their power? What would you dare to do if you believed absolutely that no agent—no person, no circumstance—can diminish or augment your reality?

Why Simples Cannot Be Needy
Argument that simples cannot be needy due to lack of possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a simple essence cannot be considered needy or dependent on an agent, based on the argument that possibility (imkan) does not apply to it.

Core Idea
A simple thing cannot be needy because it cannot admit possibility.

The author presents the first half of the sixth doubt: anything judged as needy must be either simple or composite. He argues that the simple cannot be needy because neediness is caused by possibility (imkan), and the truly simple does not admit possibility. To claim that a simple thing could possibly be itself is unintelligible. This argument aims to show that simple essences are independent of any external agent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on simples
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice how the author first states the exhaustive division (simple or composite) and then focuses on the simple.
2
Understand why simples lack possibility
The author explains that the truly simple does not admit possibility because one cannot say a thing can be itself (e.g., 'blackness can be blackness'). Possibility only arises when attributes are distinct from essence.
This is a key conceptual point.
3
Follow the logical chain
The argument: (1) Neediness requires possibility. (2) Simples do not have possibility. (3) Therefore, simples cannot be needy. Identify each step in the text.
4
Reflect on the example of blackness
The author uses blackness as an example. Notice the distinction between 'blackness can be blackness' (unintelligible) and 'blackness can persist' (valid because persistence is a separate concept).
This clarifies the nature of possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السادسة : المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة ، إما أن يكون بسيطاً ، وإما أن يكون مركباً ، والقسمان باطلان ، فالقول بالحاجة باطل ، أما الحصر فظاهر ، وإنما قلنا : إنه ممتنع أن يكون المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة بسيطاً ، وذلك لأن البسيط حقاً لا يعرض له الإمكان ، لأن من المعلوم بالضرورة أنه يستحيل الحكم على الشيء بأنه يمكن أن يكون هو هو ، فيستحيل أن يقال السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً ، بل يقال السواد يمكن أن يبقى ، ويمكن أن يحدث ، إلا أن ذلك إنما يصح لأن المفهوم [ من السواد ] (٢) مغاير للمفهوم من كونه باقياً وحادثاً ، فأما أن يقال : السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً ، فهذا غير معقول. فثبت أن الإمكان لا يعرض البتة للحقائق البسيطة ، ولما ثبت أنه لا علة للحاجة إلا الإمكان ، وثبت أن حصول الإمكان في البائط ممتنع بذلك (٣) ، ثبت أن حصول الحاجة في البسائط ممتنع . وإنما قلنا : إن المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة يمتنع أن يكون هو المركب ، وذلك لأن المركب مركب من البسائط ، فإذا كان كل واحد من تلك البسائط غنياً عن الفاعل والمؤثر ، ثم ثبت بمقتضى بديهة العقل أن عند حصول جميع المفردات ، يجب حصول المركب ، وعند فقدانها أو فقدان واحد منها يمتنع حصول المركب ، فحينئذ يلزم امتناع استناد المركبات إلى الفاعل والجاهل ، ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : المفتقر إلى المؤثر هو هيئة التركيب ؟ لأنا نقول : هيئة التركيب أحد أجزاء ماهية المركب ، فتلك الهيئة إما أن تكون مفردة أو مركبة. ويعود التقيم الأول فيه .
The sixth doubt: That which is judged to be in need of and dependent upon something else is either simple or composite, and both divisions are false, so the statement of need is false. As for the exhaustive division, it is apparent. And we only say: it is impossible for that which is judged to be in need and dependent to be simple, because the truly simple does not admit possibility (imkan), because it is necessarily known that it is impossible to judge a thing as being possibly itself. Thus it is impossible to say that blackness can be blackness. Rather, it is said that blackness can persist and can occur, except that this is valid only because the concept [of blackness] is different from the concept of its being enduring and occurring. As for saying that blackness can be blackness, this is unintelligible. So it is established that possibility (imkan) does not occur at all to simple realities. And since it is established that there is no cause for need except possibility, and it is established that the occurrence of possibility in the simple is impossible by that, it is established that the occurrence of need in simples is impossible. And we only say: that which is judged to be in need and dependent is impossible for it to be composite, because the composite is composed of simples. So when each one of those simples is independent of the agent and the doer, and then it is established by the dictate of the mind's intuition that when all the individuals are obtained, the composite must be obtained, and when they are absent or one of them is absent, the composite cannot be obtained, then at that point it follows that composites cannot be attributed to the agent and the ignorant. And it is not said: why is it not permissible to say that the one in need of the agent is the form of composition? For we say: the form of composition is one of the parts of the essence of the composite. That form is either simple or composite, and the first difficulty returns to it.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth doubt (shubha) against the need for an agent. The author argues that anything judged as needy (muftaqir) must be either simple (basit) or composite (murakkab). He then shows both possibilities are false. For the simple: the truly simple does not admit possibility (imkan), because it is impossible to say a thing can be itself (e.g., blackness can be blackness). Possibility only applies when the concept of the thing is distinct from the concept of its attributes like duration or occurrence. Since the cause of need is possibility, and the simple has no possibility, the simple cannot be needy. For the composite: composites are composed of simples, and if each simple is independent of the agent, then the composite must also be independent because whenever the parts are present, the composite necessarily exists without an agent. A potential objection that the need is in the form of composition is rejected because that form is itself either simple or composite, leading to the same dilemma.

Key Terms
بسيط (simple)
إمكان (possibility)
افتقار (neediness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Simple essences can be in need of an agent because they are possible existences.
Correction: Simples do not admit possibility at all, because possibility requires a distinction between the thing and its attributes. Therefore they cannot be needy.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that a simple thing cannot be needy?
A) Because it is composite.
B) Because it does not admit possibility (imkan).
C) Because it is eternal.
D) Because it is created.

Key Takeaway
Simple essences are not subject to possibility and therefore cannot be dependent on an agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is absolutely simple and cannot admit possibility, what does that mean for your prayers and your belief that He can change your circumstances? Do you truly rely on Him as the One who holds all attributes, or do you unconsciously treat Him as if He were contingent like yourself?
?
The author argues that 'blackness can be blackness' is unintelligible—a thing cannot be possibly itself. Reflect on your own identity: Are you tempted to say 'I am possible' or 'I could be something else'? How does this lesson's distinction between your essence and your attributes help you see that your very existence is a gift from God, not a self-standing possibility?
?
Since neediness arises only from possibility, and you are a composite being with many possibilities (to change, to sin, to repent), how does this lesson make you more aware of your constant need for God's sustaining power? Will you today acknowledge that every attribute you have—your ability to think, to move, to exist—is a distinct gift from Him, and that you are nothing without His ongoing creation?

Why Composites Cannot Be Needy
Argument that composites cannot be needy and refutation of an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why composite things cannot be needy for an agent, based on the independence of their simple parts and the refutation of the objection about the form of composition.

Core Idea
Composites cannot be needy if their simple parts are independent.

The author continues the sixth doubt by examining composite things. If a composite is made of simples, and each simple is independent of any agent, then the composite as a whole must also be independent. The argument further refutes the objection that the need lies in the 'form of composition' (hay'at al-tarkib), showing that this form is itself either simple or composite, leading to the same dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on composites
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully, focusing on the argument against composites and the objection about the form of composition.
2
Understand the logic of independence
The argument: composites are made of simples. If each simple is independent of an agent, then when all simples are present, the composite necessarily exists without any need for an external agent. This is based on intuitive reasoning.
3
Consider the objection about the form of composition
One might say that the need is in the form of composition (hay'at al-tarkib), not in the simples. The author refutes this by noting that the form itself is either simple or composite, and the same dilemma applies.
4
See the overall conclusion
The entire doubt shows that neither simples nor composites can be needy, so the claim that things need an agent is false. Reflect on how this supports the author's broader argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If composites are not needy because their parts are independent, what does that mean for your own dependence on Allah? Are you a 'composite' of independent parts, or do you rely on Him for every moment of your existence? Take a moment to genuinely feel your need for the Creator — and ask yourself: do I live as if I am self-sufficient?
?
The form of composition is not a separate entity but part of the composite's essence. In your life, do you sometimes treat your roles or achievements as separate 'forms' that you can rely on, forgetting that they are just part of a larger, dependent whole? Which 'form' in your life do you most need to surrender to Allah?
?
This argument shows that composites cannot be needy because their simples are independent. But you are neither purely simple nor purely composite — you are a created being entirely dependent on Allah. How does this truth force you to rethink the things you lean on: your health, wealth, or relationships? Write down one area where you have been acting as if you are not in need of Allah, and commit to turning back to Him today.

The Seventh Doubt: Efficacy is Not Essence
The author argues that efficacy cannot be an essence, giving three reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the effect of an agent cannot be identical to the essence of the agent, the essence of the effect, or a third concept, and the three rational reasons why this is impossible.

Core Idea
Efficacy is a relation, not an essence.

In this passage, the author presents the seventh doubt against the reality of causal efficacy. He argues that if an agent truly affects something, the act of effecting cannot be identical to the agent's essence, the effect's essence, or a distinct concept. The three reasons show that efficacy is a relation, and relations are not the things they relate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get the overall argument. Notice the three reasons introduced with 'first', 'second', 'third'.
2
Identify the three divisions
The author states that if an agent affects something, the effect (ta'thir) must be either the agent's essence, the effect's essence, or a distinct concept. All three are impossible. Find this classification in the text.
3
Examine the first reason
We can conceive both essences while doubting whether efficacy exists. This shows efficacy is not identical to either essence. How does this prove efficacy is a separate concept?
4
Examine the second and third reasons
The second reason: efficacy is a relation between two things, and a relation depends on both relata, so it is distinct from them. The third reason: different agents (fire, water) share the generic property of being agents but differ in their effects. Why do these support the argument?
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to check if you can apply the first reason correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السابعة : لو أثر شيء في شيء لكان تأثير ذلك المؤثر في ذلك الأثر ، إما أن يكون نفس ذات المؤثر [ أو ذات] (١) الأثر ، أو يكون مفهوماً مغايراً لهما ، والأقسام كلها باطلة . فالقول بالتأثير باطل ، وإنما قلنا : إن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر يمتنع أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر ، أو ذات الأثر لوجوه : الأول : إنه يمكننا أن نعقل ذات المؤثر وذات الأثر مع الشك ، في أن هذه الذات [ هل هي (٢) مؤثرة في تلك الذات ؟ مثلاً : تعقل موجوداً واجب الوجود لذاته ، وتعقل ماهية هذا العالم المحسوس ، ثم تشك في أن هذا العالم ، هل وجد بتأثير ذلك الموجود الواجب لذاته ؟ ومعلوم أن المعلوم مغاير لغير المعلوم ، فوجب أن تكون هذه المؤثرية ، مغايرة لذات المؤثر ، ولذات الأثر . الثاني : إن مؤثرية شيء في شيء ، نسبة مخصوصة لأحدهما إلى الآخر ، والنسبة بين الشيئين يتوقف تحققها على تحقق ذات كل واحد من الشيئين ، والمتوقف على الأمرين مغاير لهما ، فمؤثريه أحد الذاتين في الأخرى يجب أن تكون مغايرة لذات المؤثر وذات الأثر . الثالث : إن النار تؤثر مثلا في التسخين ، والماء يؤثر في التبريد ، فالماء والنار يتشاركان في كون كل واحد منهما مؤثراً في أثر مخصوص ، والحرارة
The seventh doubt: If one thing affected another, then the effect of that agent in that effect would either be the very essence of the agent [or the essence] of the effect, or be a concept distinct from them both, and all divisions are false. So the statement of effect is false. And we only say: the effect of the agent in the effect is impossible to be identical to the essence of the agent or the essence of the effect for several reasons: First: we can conceive the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect while doubting whether this essence is effective in that essence. For example: conceive an existent necessary of existence by itself, and conceive the essence of this sensible world, then doubt whether this world came into existence by the effect of that existent necessary by itself. And it is known that the known is distinct from what is not known, so it is necessary that this effectual relation is distinct from the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect. Second: The effectuality of one thing on another is a specific relation of one to the other, and the relation between two things depends for its realization on the realization of the essence of each of the two things, and that which depends on two things is distinct from them. So the effectuality of one of the two essences in the other must be distinct from the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect. Third: Fire, for example, affects heating, and water affects cooling. Water and fire share in that each one of them is an agent in a specific effect, and heat...
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh doubt against the efficacy of an agent. The author argues that if one thing affects another, the effect (ta'thir) cannot be identical to the essence of the agent or the effect, nor can it be a third concept distinct from both. He gives three reasons. First, we can conceive the essences of agent and effect while doubting the efficacy, which shows efficacy is distinct from those essences. Second, efficacy is a relation between two things, and a relation depends on both relata, so it is distinct from them. Third, different agents like fire and water share efficacy but have different effects, and the discussion cuts off mentioning heat. All these demonstrate that efficacy is not the same as the essences involved.

Key Terms
تأثير (effect/efficacy)
مؤثر (agent)
أثر (effect)
ذات (essence)
نسبة (relation)
مؤثرية (effectuality)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The effect of an agent is identical to the agent's essence or the effect's essence.
Correction: The author argues that efficacy is a relation distinct from both essences, as shown by the three reasons: we can doubt efficacy while knowing essences, relations depend on relata and are distinct, and different agents share the property of being agents.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason in the seventh doubt, how do we know that the effect (ta'thir) is distinct from the essences?
A) Because we can conceive the essences while doubting efficacy.
B) Because the agent must be different from the effect.
C) Because the effect is a relation.
D) Because fire and water are different.

Key Takeaway
The effect (ta'thir) is a relation between agent and effect, not identical to either essence, as demonstrated by three independent arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something, do you unconsciously attribute it to your own effort or skill? In light of this lesson's rejection of real efficacy in created things, how can you train yourself to see every outcome as directly from Allah, not from means?
?
If no created thing has any real effect, then your wealth, health, and relationships are mere occasions—what does that mean for the way you worry about them? What would it look like to genuinely entrust them to Allah?
?
The argument says we can conceive an agent without its effect. Have you ever praised or thanked someone as if they truly caused something good? How can you honor people as occasions of Allah's mercy without attributing real agency to them?

The Composite Cannot Be the Thing in Need
Sanusi argues against the composite being the dependent thing and refutes an objection about the form of composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the composite cannot be the thing in need of an agent, and how the objection about the form of composition is refuted.

Core Idea
A composite's existence depends on its parts, not an external agent.

In this passage, Sanusi delivers a tight syllogistic argument to show that the composite (مركب) cannot be that which is in need (المفتقر) of an efficient cause. He anticipates an objection regarding the 'form of composition' and demolishes it by noting that the form itself is either simple or composite, returning the argument to square one.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its translation to get an overall sense of the argument, objection, and reply.
Notice the logical connectors like 'فإذا كان', 'ثم ثبت', 'فحينئذ'.
2
Identify key terms
Identify and understand the four key terms: المفتقر (the dependent), المركب (composite), البسائط (simples), هيئة التركيب (form of composition).
These terms are essential for tracking the argument.
3
Follow the main argument
Follow Sanusi's reasoning: if all simples are independent, then the composite necessarily exists whenever they are present, so it cannot be in need of an agent.
This is the core logical move.
4
Analyze the objection and reply
Examine the objection that it is the form of composition that is in need, and see why Sanusi refutes it: the form is part of the composite's quiddity and either simple (independent) or composite (same problem).
This prevents a loophole.
5
Reflect on the lesson's importance
Consider how this argument sets the stage for discussions about causality and the ultimate dependence of all contingent things on Allah.
This connects to broader theological concerns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والحاجة يمتنع أن يكون هو المركب ، وذلك لأن المركب مركب من البسائط ، فإذا كان كل واحد من تلك البسائط غنياً عن الفاعل والمؤثر ، ثم ثبت بمقتضى بديهة العقل أن عند حصول جميع المفردات ، يجب حصول المركب ، وعند فقدانها أو فقدان واحد منها يمتنع حصول المركب ، فحينئذ يلزم امتناع استناد المركبات إلى الفاعل والجاهل ، ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : المفتقر إلى المؤثر هو هيئة التركيب ؟ لأنا نقول : هيئة التركيب أحد أجزاء ماهية المركب ، فتلك الهيئة إما أن تكون مفردة أو مركبة. ويعود التقيم الأول فيه .
That which is judged to be in need and necessity is impossible that it be the composite. That is because the composite is composed of simples. So if each of those simples is independent of the agent and the efficient cause, and then it is established by the dictate of the primary intellect that when all the individual parts are obtained, the composite must obtain, and when they are lost or one of them is lost, the composite is impossible to obtain, then at that time follows the impossibility of the composites being dependent on the agent and the ignorant. And it is not said: Why is it not permissible that it be said: The thing in need of the agent is the form of composition? For we say: The form of composition is one of the parts of the quiddity of the composite, so that form is either simple or composite, and the first estimation returns in it.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents an argument that the composite (مركب) cannot be the thing that is in need (المفتقر) of an agent. The reasoning: a composite is made of simpler parts (بسائط). If those simple parts are each independent and sufficient without an agent, then by the dictate of reason, when all simple parts are present, the composite necessarily exists, and when any part is missing, the composite cannot exist. Thus, the composite would necessarily exist whenever its parts exist, making it independent of an agent, which contradicts its being in need. An objection is raised: perhaps the thing in need is the form of composition (هيئة التركيب) rather than the composite itself. The author replies that this form is a part of the composite's quiddity, and it itself is either simple or composite; if simple, it would be independent (contradicting need), and if composite, the same argument applies, leading to infinite regress or a return to the initial estimation.

Key Terms
المفتقر
المركب
البسائط
هيئة التركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The form of composition (هيئة التركيب) might be the thing that is in need, escaping the argument against the composite.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the form of composition is a part of the composite's quiddity; if it is simple, it is independent like other simples, and if composite, the same argument applies, so it cannot be in need either.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why cannot the composite be the thing in need of an agent?
A) Because the composite is more perfect than its parts.
B) Because if all simple parts are independent, the composite would necessarily exist when they are present, contradicting its need.
C) Because the composite is eternal.
D) Because the agent cannot act on composites.

Key Takeaway
A composite cannot be in need because its existence follows necessarily from its parts; the form of composition fails as an alternative because it too is either simple (independent) or composite (same problem).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi shows that a composite's existence necessarily follows from its parts. In your life, what 'parts' (habits, relationships, achievements) have you allowed to define your existence, and have you realized that your ultimate need is not in those parts but in the Agent who gives them being? How can you reprioritize so that your reliance is on Allah alone?
?
The form of composition is part of the quiddity—something internal, not external. Where do you look for the 'missing piece' in your spirituality? Have you been seeking external fixes (more knowledge, more practice) while ignoring that the very structure of your being is dependent on the Creator? What would change if you lived from that internal need?
?
Sanusi argues that the composite cannot be the thing in need because its existence is necessitated by its parts. Are you living as though your spiritual life is 'necessitated' by external factors—a particular teacher, a specific community—rather than recognizing that you, in your essence, are in need of Allah? What step can you take today to realign your sense of dependence?

The Seventh Doubt and the Distinction of Causality from the Agent's Essence
Sanusi presents the seventh doubt and gives four proofs that causality is distinct from the agent's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's four proofs that the causal relation is a concept distinct from the agent's essence, refuting the first part of the seventh doubt.

Core Idea
Causality is a concept distinct from the agent itself, not identical to it.

The seventh doubt argues that causation is impossible by assuming the effect must be either the agent's essence, the effect's essence, or a distinct concept—then rejecting all three. Sanusi begins his response by showing that causality cannot be identical to the agent's essence. This lesson covers his first four proofs that establish causality as an additional concept over and above the agent's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt and grasp the assumption
Read the opening lines that lay out the three possibilities and the doubt's conclusion. Notice the structure: the doubt asserts all divisions are false, so causation is invalid.
Sanusi will refute each division.
2
Follow the first two proofs
Examine proof 1 (conceivability while doubting) and proof 2 (causality as a relation). Note how each shows causality is additional to the essence.
Proof 1 uses the example of the Necessary Being and the world.
3
Analyze the third and fourth proofs
Proof 3 uses fire/water to show sharing in agency despite different essences. Proof 4 contrasts 'Power of God' repeated versus 'Power of God effective in the world' to show added meaning.
Proof 4 is especially clear: the second phrase gives information the first does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السابعة : لو أثر شيء في شيء لكان تأثير ذلك المؤثر في ذلك الأثر ، إما أن يكون نفس ذات المؤثر [ أو ذات] الأثر ، أو يكون مفهوماً مغايراً لهما ، والأقسام كلها باطلة . فالقول بالتأثير باطل ، وإنما قلنا : إن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر يمتنع أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر ، أو ذات الأثر لوجوه : الأول : إنه يمكننا أن نعقل ذات المؤثر وذات الأثر مع الشك ، في أن هذه الذات [ هل هي] مؤثرة في تلك الذات؟ مثلاً : تعقل موجوداً واجب الوجود لذاته ، وتعقل ماهية هذا العالم المحسوس ، ثم تشك في أن هذا العالم ، هل وجد بتأثير ذلك الموجود الواجب لذاته ؟ ومعلوم أن المعلوم مغاير لغير المعلوم ، فوجب أن تكون هذه المؤثرية ، مغايرة لذات المؤثر ، ولذات الأثر . الثاني : إن مؤثرية شيء في شيء ، نسبة مخصوصة لأحدهما إلى الآخر ، والنسبة بين الشيئين يتوقف تحققها على تحقق ذات كل واحد من الشيئين ، والمتوقف على الأمرين مغاير لهما ، فمؤثريه أحد الذاتين في الأخرى يجب أن تكون مغايرة لذات المؤثر وذات الأثر . الثالث : إن النار تؤثر مثلا في التسخين ، والماء يؤثر في التبريد ، فالماء والنار يتشاركان في كون كل واحد منهما مؤثراً في أثر مخصوص ، والحرارة والبرودة يتشاركان في كون كل واحد منهما أثراً لمؤثر مخصوص ، فثبت أن المشاركة في مفهوم المؤثرية وفي مفهوم الأثرية حاصلة . وأما المشاركة في خصوص ذات المؤثر وخصوص ذات الأثر فغير حاصلة ، فإن ذات النار مخالفة لذات الماء ، وحقيقة الحرارة مخالفة لحقيقة [ البرودة ، وإذا ثبت هذا ، لزم القطع بأن كون النار مؤثرة غير ، وكونها ناراً غير ، وكذلك] كون الحرارة أثراً لمؤثر غير ، وكونها حرارة غير. الرابع : إنا إذا قلنا : قدرة الله ، قدرة الله . فهذا الكلام عبث لا يفيد فائدة ، أما إذا قلنا : قدرة الله مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، كان هذا الكلام مفيداً فلو كان المفهوم من كون القدرة قدرة ، غير المفهوم من كونها مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، وجب أن لا يبقى البتة فرق بين الكلامين ، فظهر بهذا البرهان : أن التأثير مفهوم مغاير لذات المؤثر . بقي أن نقيم البرهان على أن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ليس عين ذات الأثر ، فنقول : الذي يدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنا إذا قلنا قدرة الله مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، كنا قد وصفنا قدرة الله تعالى بهذه المؤثرية، ومعلوم بالضرورة أن العالم ليس صفة لقدرة الله ، ويلزم من مجموع هاتين المقدمتين القطع بأن قدرة الله تعالى في العالم ليست نفس العالم . الوجه الثاني في إبطال هذا الكلام : أنه إذا قيل لنا : لم وجد العالم ؟ كان جوابنا : إن قدرة الله تعالى اقتضت إيجاد العالم في الوجود ، [ فعللنا وجود العالم في الوجود] بأن الله تعالى أوجده ، فلو كان إيجاد الله للعالم عين العالم ، لكان قولنا : العالم إنما وجد بإيجاد الله تعالى معناه : أن العالم إنما وجد بنفسه ، ولو وجد العالم بنفسه لامتنع أن يقال : إنه وجد بإيجاد الله تعالى ، فثبت أنا لو فسرنا تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ، بنفس وجود ذلك الأثر ، لزم نفي المؤثر ونفي
The seventh doubt: If something were to affect something, then the effect of that agent in that effect must be either the very essence of the agent [or the essence] of the effect, or a concept distinct from them, and all the divisions are invalid. So the claim of causation is invalid. And we only say: The effect of the agent in the effect is impossible to be identical to the essence of the agent, or to the essence of the effect, for several reasons. First: It is possible for us to conceive the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect while being in doubt about whether this essence [is] effective upon that essence. For example: conceive an existent necessary by itself, and conceive the quiddity of this perceived world, then doubt whether this world came to be by the effect of that existent necessary by itself. And it is known that the known is distinct from the unknown, so necessarily this causality must be distinct from the essence of the agent and from the essence of the effect. Second: The causality of a thing in another thing is a specific relation of one to the other, and the relation between two things depends for its actualization on the actualization of the essence of each of the two things, and that which depends on two things is distinct from them, so the causality of one of the two essences in the other must be distinct from the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect. Third: Fire heats, for example, and water cools. Water and fire share in each being an agent in a specific effect, and heat and cold share in each being an effect of a specific agent. So it is established that sharing in the concept of agency and in the concept of effectness obtains. As for sharing in the particular essence of the agent and the particular essence of the effect, it does not obtain; for the essence of fire is different from the essence of water, and the reality of heat is different from the reality of [cold. And when this is established, it necessarily follows that fire's being an agent is other than its being fire, and likewise] heat's being an effect of an agent is other than its being heat. Fourth: If we say 'power of God, power of God', this speech is futile and yields no benefit. But if we say 'the power of God is effective in the existence of the world', this speech is beneficial. If the concept of power being power were not different from the concept of its being effective in the existence of the world, then there would be no difference at all between the two statements. Thus it appears from this proof that effect is a concept distinct from the essence of the agent. It remains for us to present the proof that the effect of the agent in the effect is not identical to the essence of the effect. We say: That which indicates it are several aspects. First: We say 'the power of God is effective in the existence of the world', we have described the power of God most high with this effectiveness, and it is known necessarily that the world is not an attribute of the power of God. From the conjunction of these two premises, it necessarily follows that the power of God most high in the world is not the world itself. The second aspect in refuting this statement: If it were said to us: Why did the world exist? Our answer would be: The power of God most high required the bringing of the world into existence, [so we caused the existence of the world into existence] by God most high bringing it into existence. If bringing the world into existence by God were identical to the world, then our saying 'the world only came to be by God's bringing it into existence' would mean that the world came to be by itself. And if the world came to be by itself, it would be impossible to say that it came to be by God's bringing it into existence. So it is established that if we interpret the effect of the agent in the effect as being the very existence of that effect, then the negation of the agent and the negation
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh doubt (الشبهة السابعة) in the debate on causality. The doubt claims that causation is impossible because the effect of an agent on an effect must be either identical to the agent's essence, identical to the effect's essence, or a distinct concept. The doubt argues that all three are false, so causation is invalid. The author Sanusi responds by proving that it is indeed a distinct concept. He gives four proofs that the effect is not identical to the agent's essence: (1) We can conceive both essences while doubting the causality relation, so causality is an additional notion. (2) Causality is a relation, and a relation between two things is distinct from the things themselves. (3) Different agents (fire and water) share the concept of agency despite differing essences, and different effects share the concept of effectness — thus causality is a universal concept distinct from particular essences. (4) The phrase 'power of God, power of God' is useless, but 'power of God is effective in the existence of the world' is informative, so 'effectiveness' adds meaning beyond 'power'. The author then transitions to prove that the effect is also not identical to the effect's essence. He gives two proofs: (1) When we say 'God's power is effective in the world', we describe the power with effectiveness, but the world is not an attribute of power; thus the power is not the world. (2) If we explain the world's existence by God's bringing it into existence, then if that bringing were identical to the world, it would mean the world brought itself into existence, which contradicts its dependence on God. The second proof is cut off at the end of the page.

Key Terms
الشبهة السابعة
تأثير
مؤثر
أثر
ذات
مفهوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that causation is impossible because the effect must be either identical to the agent or to the effect, and both are impossible.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the effect is neither identical to the agent's essence nor to the effect's essence, but a distinct relational concept; thus causation is possible.

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the fourth proof that causality is distinct from the agent's essence?
A) Fire and water share the concept of agency.
B) The phrase 'power of God' is less informative than 'power of God effective in the world'.
C) We can conceive agent and effect while doubting causality.
D) Causality is a relation between two things.

Key Takeaway
Causality is a relational concept distinct from the agent's essence, as shown by four proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience something good or bad, do you attribute it to some 'cause' like your effort or luck, forgetting that the very concept of causality is a distinct relation created by God? How can you remind yourself that every effect is directly from Him?
?
The fourth proof shows that saying 'power of God' without affirming its effect is futile. Are there aspects of your life where you profess belief in God's power but live as if your own power is sufficient? What one change can you make today to align your actions with the truth that His power is effective in your daily existence?

Causality and Created Things
beginner
4 min
Proofs that Causality is Not Identical to the Effect's Essence
Sanusi gives two proofs that causality is not the effect's essence, completing the refutation of the seventh doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's two proofs that the causal effect is not identical to the effect's essence, completing the refutation of the seventh doubt.

Core Idea
The effect of an agent is not the same as the existence of the effect itself.

Having proven that causality is not identical to the agent's essence, Sanusi now addresses the second possibility: that the effect (the causal influence) might be identical to the effect's essence (the thing affected). He gives two proofs, the second of which is cut off in the manuscript. This lesson covers the first complete proof and the beginning of the second.

Guided Path
1
Read the transition and the first proof
Start from 'It remains for us...'. The first proof argues: when we say 'God's power is effective in the world', we describe the power with effectiveness, but the world is not an attribute of God's power; thus the effectiveness is not the world itself.
Notice the logical structure: two premises lead to the conclusion.
2
Examine the second proof (incomplete)
The second proof uses a conditional: if bringing the world into existence were identical to the world, then explaining the world's existence by God's bringing would mean the world caused itself—a contradiction. The proof is cut off but the reasoning is clear.
The missing conclusion would state that causality cannot be the effect itself.
3
Reflect on the overall refutation
With both sets of proofs, Sanusi has shown that causality is a distinct concept from both the agent and the effect, thereby answering the seventh doubt.
The doubt's trilemma is resolved: causality is the third option—a distinct concept.

The seventh doubt: If something were to affect something, then the effect of that agent in that effect must be either the very essence of the agent [or the essence] of the effect, or a concept distinct from them, and all the divisions are invalid. So the claim of causation is invalid. And we only say: The effect of the agent in the effect is impossible to be identical to the essence of the agent, or to the essence of the effect, for several reasons. First: It is possible for us to conceive the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect while being in doubt about whether this essence [is] effective upon that essence. For example: conceive an existent necessary by itself, and conceive the quiddity of this perceived world, then doubt whether this world came to be by the effect of that existent necessary by itself. And it is known that the known is distinct from the unknown, so necessarily this causality must be distinct from the essence of the agent and from the essence of the effect. Second: The causality of a thing in another thing is a specific relation of one to the other, and the relation between two things depends for its actualization on the actualization of the essence of each of the two things, and that which depends on two things is distinct from them, so the causality of one of the two essences in the other must be distinct from the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect. Third: Fire heats, for example, and water cools. Water and fire share in each being an agent in a specific effect, and heat and cold share in each being an effect of a specific agent. So it is established that sharing in the concept of agency and in the concept of effectness obtains. As for sharing in the particular essence of the agent and the particular essence of the effect, it does not obtain; for the essence of fire is different from the essence of water, and the reality of heat is different from the reality of [cold. And when this is established, it necessarily follows that fire's being an agent is other than its being fire, and likewise] heat's being an effect of an agent is other than its being heat. Fourth: If we say 'power of God, power of God', this speech is futile and yields no benefit. But if we say 'the power of God is effective in the existence of the world', this speech is beneficial. If the concept of power being power were not different from the concept of its being effective in the existence of the world, then there would be no difference at all between the two statements. Thus it appears from this proof that effect is a concept distinct from the essence of the agent. It remains for us to present the proof that the effect of the agent in the effect is not identical to the essence of the effect. We say: That which indicates it are several aspects. First: We say 'the power of God is effective in the existence of the world', we have described the power of God most high with this effectiveness, and it is known necessarily that the world is not an attribute of the power of God. From the conjunction of these two premises, it necessarily follows that the power of God most high in the world is not the world itself. The second aspect in refuting this statement: If it were said to us: Why did the world exist? Our answer would be: The power of God most high required the bringing of the world into existence, [so we caused the existence of the world into existence] by God most high bringing it into existence. If bringing the world into existence by God were identical to the world, then our saying 'the world only came to be by God's bringing it into existence' would mean that the world came to be by itself. And if the world came to be by itself, it would be impossible to say that it came to be by God's bringing it into existence. So it is established that if we interpret the effect of the agent in the effect as being the very existence of that effect, then the negation of the agent and the negation
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh doubt (الشبهة السابعة) in the debate on causality. The doubt claims that causation is impossible because the effect of an agent on an effect must be either identical to the agent's essence, identical to the effect's essence, or a distinct concept. The doubt argues that all three are false, so causation is invalid. The author Sanusi responds by proving that it is indeed a distinct concept. He gives four proofs that the effect is not identical to the agent's essence: (1) We can conceive both essences while doubting the causality relation, so causality is an additional notion. (2) Causality is a relation, and a relation between two things is distinct from the things themselves. (3) Different agents (fire and water) share the concept of agency despite differing essences, and different effects share the concept of effectness — thus causality is a universal concept distinct from particular essences. (4) The phrase 'power of God, power of God' is useless, but 'power of God is effective in the existence of the world' is informative, so 'effectiveness' adds meaning beyond 'power'. The author then transitions to prove that the effect is also not identical to the effect's essence. He gives two proofs: (1) When we say 'God's power is effective in the world', we describe the power with effectiveness, but the world is not an attribute of power; thus the power is not the world. (2) If we explain the world's existence by God's bringing it into existence, then if that bringing were identical to the world, it would mean the world brought itself into existence, which contradicts its dependence on God. The second proof is cut off at the end of the page.

The causal effect is a concept distinct from the effect's essence; identifying them would lead to logical contradictions.

Effect Is Distinct from the Agent's Essence
Author proves effect is distinct from agent's essence using examples and argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the concept of effect (ta'thir) is considered distinct from the essence of the cause in classical kalam.

Core Idea
Effectiveness is an added meaning, not the essence itself.

This lesson unpacks a foundational proof in kalam: that the effect an agent produces is not identical to the agent's essence. The author uses two clear arguments—one from shared attributes of opposites, and one from the difference between repetition and meaningful predication—to show that 'being effective' is a distinct concept from 'being what it is.' Understanding this distinction is crucial for later discussions on divine attributes and causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice how the author moves from an example to a direct linguistic argument.
The passage uses a 'fourth' (الرابع) label, indicating this is part of a longer enumeration.
2
Analyze the first argument: heat and cold
Identify how the author uses heat and cold to show that two effects can share the concept of being an effect while having different essences. This suggests that 'effectiveness' is separate from the essence of the cause or effect.
Fire and water are distinct essences, yet both produce effects (heat and cold) that share the concept of being effects.
3
Analyze the second argument: repetition vs. predication
Consider the difference between 'power of God, power of God' (futile) and 'power of God is effective in the existence of the world' (beneficial). Why does adding 'effective in the existence of the world' add meaning?
If effectiveness were the same as power, both sentences would be equivalent—but they are not.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
Combine both arguments to see that the author has proven: effect (ta'thir) is a concept distinct from the essence of the agent. Ask yourself: why is this important for kalam?
This distinction allows for a richer discussion of divine attributes and causality.

والبرودة يتشاركان في كون كل واحد منهما أثراً لمؤثر مخصوص ، فثبت أن المشاركة في مفهوم المؤثرية وفي مفهوم الأثرية حاصلة . وأما المشاركة في خصوص ذات المؤثر وخصوص ذات الأثر فغير حاصلة ، فإن ذات النار مخالفة لذات الماء ، وحقيقة الحرارة مخالفة لحقيقة البرودة ، وإذا ثبت هذا ، لزم القطع بأن كون النار مؤثرة غير ، وكونها ناراً غير ، وكذلك كون الحرارة أثراً لمؤثر غير ، وكونها حرارة غير. الرابع : إنا إذا قلنا : قدرة الله ، قدرة الله . فهذا الكلام عبث لا يفيد فائدة ، أما إذا قلنا : قدرة الله مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، كان هذا الكلام مفيداً فلو كان المفهوم من كون القدرة قدرة ، غير المفهوم من كونها مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، وجب أن لا يبقى البتة فرق بين الكلامين ، فظهر بهذا البرهان : أن التأثير مفهوم مغاير لذات المؤثر.
Both heat and cold share in that each one of them is an effect of a specific cause. So it is established that sharing in the concept of causality (al-mu'thiriyya) and in the concept of effect (al-athariyya) occurs. As for sharing in the particular essence of the cause and the particular essence of the effect, it does not occur. For the essence of fire is contrary to the essence of water, and the reality of heat is contrary to the reality of cold. And if this is established, it necessarily follows that the fire being effective is other than its being fire, and likewise that heat being an effect of a cause is other than its being heat. Fourth: If we say 'power of God, power of God,' this speech is futile, conveying no benefit. But if we say 'power of God is effective in the existence of the world,' this speech is beneficial. And if the concept of power being power were other than the concept of it being effective in the existence of the world, there would necessarily be no difference at all between the two statements. So by this proof it is shown that effect (al-ta'thir) is a concept distinct from the essence of the cause.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the concept of effect (ta'thir) is distinct from the essence of the agent. The author presents two arguments: (1) heat and cold are both effects of specific causes (fire and water), but they share the concepts of causality and effect without sharing the essences of the causes or the effects themselves; thus, being effective or being an effect is separate from the essence. (2) The linguistic argument: repeating 'power of God' is meaningless, but saying 'power of God is effective in the existence of the world' is informative, so effectiveness must be an added meaning beyond the essence of power. Therefore, the effect is a distinct concept.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'effectiveness' is just another name for the agent's essence, so saying 'God's power' already implies effectiveness.
Correction: The passage shows that if effectiveness were identical to essence, then repeating 'God's power' would be as meaningful as adding 'effective', which it is not. Therefore, effectiveness is a separate concept.
