Key Takeaway
The concept of effect (ta'thir) is a distinct attribute added to the essence of the agent, not identical to it.

First Proof: The Effect is Not the Essence
First proof that the effect is not identical to the effect's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical distinction between an agent's effectiveness and the effect itself, and why the world cannot be an attribute of God's power.

Core Idea
The effect is not the same as the action that produces it.

The first proof focuses on a simple but critical distinction: when we say God's power is effective, that effectiveness is a description of the power, not of the effect. The effect (the world) is something else entirely. This lesson walks through the two premises that establish this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis being argued
Read the passage to understand what the author is trying to prove: that the effect of the agent on the effect is not identical to the essence of the effect.
The thesis is stated at the beginning: 'It remains for us to establish the proof...'
2
Analyze the first premise
When we say 'God's power is effective in the existence of the world,' we are attributing effectiveness to God's power, not to the world. Recognize that this premise describes the power itself.
Effectiveness is a description (attribute) of the power.
3
Understand the second premise and conclusion
The second premise states that the world is not an attribute of God's power. Since effectiveness is an attribute of God's power, and the world is not, effectiveness cannot be the world. Therefore, the effect (ta'thir) is distinct from the world.
The conclusion follows necessarily from the two premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي أن نقيم البرهان على أن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ليس عين ذات الأثر ، فنقول : الذي يدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إنا إذا قلنا قدرة الله مؤثرة في وجود العالم ، كنا قد وصفنا قدرة الله تعالى بهذه المؤثرية، ومعلوم بالضرورة أن العالم ليس صفة لقدرة الله ، ويلزم من مجموع هاتين المقدمتين القطع بأن قدرة الله تعالى في العالم ليست نفس العالم .
It remains for us to establish the proof that the effect of the agent on the effect is not identical to the essence of the effect. We say: what indicates this are [several] aspects: The first: If we say 'the power of God is effective in the existence of the world,' we have described God's power with this effectiveness. And it is known by necessity that the world is not an attribute of God's power. And from the combination of these two premises, it necessarily follows that the effectiveness of God's power in the world is not the world itself.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage introduces the proof that the effect (ta'thir) is not identical to the essence of the effect. The author states that we need to prove this, and then gives the first proof. The proof consists of two premises: (1) When we say 'God's power is effective in the existence of the world,' we are describing God's power with the attribute of effectiveness. (2) It is self-evident that the world is not an attribute of God's power. Therefore, the effectiveness (which is an attribute of God's power) cannot be the world itself. Thus, the effect is distinct from the effect's essence.

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of God's power is an attribute of the power, not the world itself, so the effect (the act of affecting) is distinct from the effect (the world).

Second Proof: Identification Would Negate Agent and Effect
Second proof via reductio that effect is not identical to the act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio argument demonstrating that the act of creation cannot be identical to the created thing, because that would lead to self-causation and negation of both cause and effect.

Core Idea
If the act of creation were the thing itself, the thing would be self-created, which is absurd.

This passage presents a crucial argument in Islamic theology about causality. It shows why the act of bringing into existence must be distinct from the thing brought into existence. The proof is a simple but powerful reductio ad absurdum that exposes the logical fallacy of identifying cause with effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Pay attention to the conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
Notice how the argument begins with a hypothetical scenario.
2
Identify the conditional scenario
The passage considers the scenario where the act of bringing into existence (إيجاد) is identical to the world itself. Identify this assumption.
3
Trace the logical chain to absurdity
Follow the reasoning: if act = world, then explaining the world by the act means the world exists by itself. Then if self-existent, it cannot be said to exist by God's act. This leads to negation of both the agent (God) and the effect (world).
The conclusion is that the original identification leads to its own negation.
4
Draw the conclusion
The argument concludes that the statement 'the effect of the agent on the effect is identical to that effect' is false. Understand why this rejection is necessary for affirming causality.
This proof reinforces the distinction between God's act and the created world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في إبطال هذا الكلام : أنه إذا قيل لنا : لم وجد العالم ؟ كان جوابنا : إن قدرة الله تعالى اقتضت إيجاد العالم في الوجود ، فعللنا وجود العالم في الوجود بأن الله تعالى أوجده ، فلو كان إيجاد الله للعالم عين العالم ، لكان قولنا : العالم إنما وجد بإيجاد الله تعالى معناه : أن العالم إنما وجد بنفسه ، ولو وجد العالم بنفسه لامتنع أن يقال : إنه وجد بإيجاد الله تعالى ، فثبت أنا لو فسرنا تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ، بنفس وجود ذلك الأثر ، لزم نفي المؤثر ونفي الأثر ، وما أفضى ثبوته إلى نفيه ، كان باطلاً فوجب أن يكون القول بأن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر نفس ذلك الأثر : قولاً باطلاً.
The second aspect in refuting this statement: that if it is said to us: 'Why did the world exist?' our answer would be: 'God's power necessitated bringing the world into existence.' So we have caused the existence of the world in existence by the fact that God brought it into existence. If God's bringing the world into existence were identical to the world, then our saying 'the world only came into existence by God's bringing it into existence' would mean that the world only came into existence by itself. And if the world came into existence by itself, it would be impossible to say that it came into existence by God's bringing it into existence. So it is established that if we interpret the effect of the agent on the effect as the very existence of that effect, it would necessitate the negation of the agent and the negation of the effect. And whatever leads from its affirmation to its negation is false. So necessarily, the statement that the effect of the agent on the effect is identical to that effect is a false statement.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof that the effect is not identical to the effect's essence. The proof is a reductio ad absurdum: If God's bringing into existence (the act of creation) were identical to the world itself, then explaining the world's existence by saying 'God brought it into existence' would be equivalent to saying 'the world existed by itself.' But if the world existed by itself, we could no longer attribute its existence to God's act. This leads to the absurd conclusion that both the agent (God) and the effect (the world) are negated, since there would be no act of bringing into existence and the world would be self-sufficient. Therefore, the act (ta'thir) cannot be identical to the effect.

Key Terms
إيجاد
نفي
مؤثر
أثر
تعليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the act of creation is just another word for the created thing itself.
Correction: The act of creation is a distinct entity; identifying them leads to self-causation and logical absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, if God's act of bringing into existence were identical to the world itself, what would necessarily follow?
A) The world would be eternal.
B) The world would have come into existence by itself.
C) God would be identical to the world.
D) The world would be an attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
The act of creation is not identical to the creation; otherwise the latter would be self-sufficient and the agent would be denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your very existence at this moment is due to a distinct, continuous act of God, or do you sometimes feel self-sufficient? What would change in your daily life if you fully internalised that you are never independent of God's creative act?
?
When you achieve something or avoid harm, do you attribute it to your own power and planning, implicitly denying God's distinct agency? How can you consciously affirm that God's act is separate from the outcome?
?
The passage warns that confusing the act with the effect negates both. In your relationship with God, are there areas where you treat His blessings as if they are self-originating or automatic? How can you re-establish the correct attitude of total dependence?

Third and Fourth Proofs: Effectiveness as a Relational Concept
Third and fourth proofs establishing effect as a third concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the effect (ta'thir) cannot be identical to the essence of the agent or the essence of the effect, and why it must be a third relational concept.

Core Idea
Effectiveness is not a substance but a relational third concept.

In the previous proofs, the author established that the effect cannot be the agent's essence. Now, he presents two more arguments to show that the effect is not the effect's own essence either, and that it belongs to the category of relation (مضاف). These arguments further clarify the distinct nature of causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: third proof, fourth proof, then a conclusion.
2
Understand the third proof
The third proof presents a dilemma: God's bringing into existence (إيجاد) either refers to the world itself or to the world's issuing from God's power. The first option is impossible because it would imply the world is self-existent or dependent on another other than God. Thus, it must be the second option, which is distinct from both the world and power.
This shows that the effect is a third concept.
3
Understand the fourth proof
The fourth proof observes that being an agent and being an effect are relational terms (مضاف). The essences themselves are not relational. Therefore, effectiveness cannot be identical to either essence.
Relational terms are not substances.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that all four proofs together establish that effectiveness is a third concept distinct from the essences. Consider how this supports the overall argument against the identity of cause and effect.
This is a key point in Sunni kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث في إبطال هذا الكلام : إما أن نفسر إيجاد الله تعالى للعالم بنفس العالم ، وإما أن نفسره لا بنفس العالم ، بل بصدور العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، والأول باطل ، لأن بتقدير أن يوجد العالم لذاته ، أو يوجد بإيجاد موجود آخر غير الله ، لم يصح القول بأن العالم حصل بإيجاد الله تعالى ، فثبت أن إيجاد الله تعالى للعالم لا يمكن تفسيره بنفس العالم ، وإنما يمكن تفسيره بوقوع العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، وعند هذا نقول : ظهر أن كون العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، مغاير لذات العالم ، ولذات القدرة فوجب أن يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً فثبت أن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ، لا يجوز أن يكون نفس ذات المؤثر ، ولا يجوز أن يكون نفس ذات الأثر ، فوجب أن يكون أمراً مغايراً لهما . والوجه الرابع في بيان أن تأثير الشيء في الشيء، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر وعين الأثر : هو أن كون المؤثر مؤثراً في الأثر ، وكون الأثر أثراً للمؤثر من مقولة المضاف، وأما ذات المؤثر وذات الأثر فليسا كذلك. لأنا إذا قلنا : إن الله تعالى خلق العالم ، فذات المؤثر هي ذات واجب الوجود ، وذات الأثر هو ذات العالم . فثبت بهذه البراهين الأربعة : أنه لو أثر شيء في شيء، لكانت مؤثرية أحدهما في الآخر ليست عين ذات المؤثر، ولا عين ذات الأثر ، بل كانت مفهوماً ثالثاً مغايراً لهما . وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يقال المفهوم من المؤثرية مفهوم ثالث مغاير لذات المؤثر ولذات الأثر
The third aspect in refuting this statement: either we interpret God's bringing the world into existence as the world itself, or we interpret it not as the world itself but as the world's issuing from God's power. The first is false, because if the world were to exist by itself, or exist by the bringing into existence of another existent other than God, it would not be correct to say that the world occurred by God's bringing into existence. So it is established that God's bringing the world into existence cannot be interpreted as the world itself, but can only be interpreted as the world's occurring from God's power. And at this point we say: it appears that the world being from God's power is distinct from the essence of the world and from the essence of power, so it must be a third concept. So it is established that the effect of the agent on the effect cannot be identical to the essence of the agent, nor can it be identical to the essence of the effect, so it must be something distinct from both. The fourth aspect in clarifying that the effect of a thing in a thing is impossible to be identical to the essence of the agent and identical to the essence of the effect: that the agent being effective in the effect and the effect being an effect of the agent are from the category of relative terms (al-mudaf), whereas the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect are not like that. For if we say 'God created the world,' then the essence of the agent is the essence of the Necessary Existent, and the essence of the effect is the essence of the world. So it is established by these four proofs that if a thing affects a thing, the effectiveness of one in the other is not identical to the essence of the agent, nor identical to the essence of the effect, but rather is a third concept distinct from both. And as for the second division, it is that it is said: the concept of effectiveness is a third concept distinct from the essence of the agent and the essence of the effect.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth proofs and concludes the overall argument. The third proof: the act of bringing into existence (إيجاد) must be interpreted either as the world itself (impossible, because then the world would be self-existent and not dependent on God) or as the world's issuing from God's power (which is a distinct concept). Therefore, the effect is a third concept separate from both the agent and the effect. The fourth proof: effectiveness is a relational concept (مضاف) — 'being effective' and 'being an effect' are relation terms, while the essences of agent and effect are not relational. Therefore, they cannot be identical. The conclusion from all four proofs: the effect (ta'thir) is a third concept distinct from both essences. The author then transitions to the second division, which is the statement that the concept of effectiveness is a third concept distinct from both.

Correction: The author argues that effectiveness is a third concept (مفهوم ثالث) that is distinct from both the agent and the effect, and it belongs to the category of relation (مضاف), which is a real category.

Key Takeaway
Effectiveness is not the essence of agent or effect but a distinct relational concept.

The Third Proof: Effect Is a Third Concept
Al-Razi presents the third proof that efficacy is distinct from cause and effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi's third argument proves that the efficacy of a cause is a third concept distinct from both the cause and the effect.

Core Idea
The effect of a cause is neither the cause nor the effect; it's a third thing.

This passage presents a key proof in Islamic philosophical theology about causation. Al-Razi argues that God's act of creating the world cannot be identical to the world itself. Instead, it must be something else—a distinct reality that is neither God's essence nor the world's essence. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source text
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the flow of the argument.
Notice the disjunction at the beginning: either interpretation A or B.
2
Analyze the disjunction
Identify the two options al-Razi presents for interpreting God's bringing-into-existence (ījād).
The first option equates ījād with the world's essence; the second with the world's proceeding from God's power.
3
Understand why the first option fails
Al-Razi argues that if the world existed by itself or by another cause, it couldn't be attributed to God. Thus the first option is false.
This step relies on common theological presuppositions that only God creates.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The second option is true, so the world's being from God's power is a third concept, distinct from both the world's essence and God's power.
This proves that efficacy is a third reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث في إبطال هذا الكلام : إما أن نفسر إيجاد الله تعالى للعالم بنفس العالم ، وإما أن نفسره لا بنفس العالم ، بل بصدور العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، والأول باطل ، لأن بتقدير أن يوجد العالم لذاته ، أو يوجد بإيجاد موجود آخر غير الله ، لم يصح القول بأن العالم حصل بإيجاد الله تعالى ، فثبت أن إيجاد الله تعالى للعالم لا يمكن تفسيره بنفس العالم ، وإنما يمكن تفسيره بوقوع العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، وعند هذا نقول : ظهر أن كون العالم من قدرة الله تعالى ، مغاير لذات العالم ، ولذات القدرة فوجب أن يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً فثبت أن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر ، لا يجوز أن يكون نفس ذات المؤثر ، ولا يجوز أن يكون نفس ذات الأثر ، فوجب أن يكون أمراً مغايراً لهما .
The third argument in invalidating this statement: either we interpret the bringing-into-existence (ījād) of God, exalted, for the world as the very essence of the world, or we interpret it not as the very essence of the world but as the world's proceeding from God's power. The first is false because, on the assumption that the world exists by itself or exists by the bringing-into-existence of another existent other than God, it would not be correct to say that the world came about by God's bringing-into-existence. Thus it is established that God's bringing-into-existence for the world cannot be interpreted as the very essence of the world, but can only be interpreted as the world's occurring from God's power. At this point we say: it becomes apparent that the world's being from God's power is other than the essence of the world and other than the essence of power, so it must be a third concept. Thus it is established that the effect (ta'thīr) of the cause (mu'aththir) upon the effect (athar) cannot be the very essence of the cause, nor can it be the very essence of the effect, so it must be something other than both.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents the third of four proofs that the efficacy (ta'thīr) of a cause upon its effect is neither identical to the cause's essence nor the effect's essence, but a distinct third concept. The argument proceeds as a disjunction: either God's act of creating the world is identical to the world's essence, or it is not. The first option is false because if the world existed by itself or by another cause, it would not be correct to attribute its existence to God. Therefore, God's bringing-into-existence is not the world's essence; rather, it is the world's proceeding from God's power. This proceeding is distinct from both the world's essence and God's power, proving that efficacy is a third concept.

Key Terms
إيجاد (ījād)
قدرة (qudra)
تأثير (ta'thīr)
مؤثر (mu'aththir)
أثر (athar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that the act of creation is identical to the created world itself.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that if ījād were the world's essence, the world could exist by itself or by another cause, making divine attribution incoherent. Therefore, ījād must be a distinct reality.

Checkpoint
According to the third argument, why is it false to interpret God's bringing-into-existence (ījād) as the very essence of the world?
A) Because the world is eternal and not created.
B) Because if the world existed by itself or by another cause, it would not be correct to attribute its existence to God.
C) Because God's power is identical to the world.
D) Because the world cannot proceed from God's power.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's third argument proves that the effect of a cause is a distinct reality, neither the cause nor the effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Efficacy as a Third Concept: The Fourth Proof
Al-Razi gives the fourth proof and concludes that efficacy is a third concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument that causality (efficacy) is a relational concept distinct from the essences of cause and effect, and how this concludes that efficacy is a third concept.

Core Idea
Efficacy is not part of the essence of cause or effect; it is a relation between them.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents the fourth and final proof that efficacy (mu'aththariyya) cannot be identical to the essence of the cause or the effect. He then concludes that all four proofs together establish that efficacy is a third, distinct concept. We will see how the argument from relationality (al-muḍāf) solidifies this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from al-Razi carefully, then the literal English translation. Notice the key terms: المؤثر (cause), الأثر (effect), المضاف (relation).
2
Identify the argument from relation
Al-Razi argues that 'the cause's being a cause' and 'the effect's being an effect' belong to the category of relation (al-muḍāf), but the essences themselves are not relations. Therefore, efficacy cannot be identical to either essence.
3
Consider the example of God creating the world
When God creates the world, His essence is the Necessary Existent, and the world's essence is the world. These essences are not relational. So efficacy must be something else.
4
Understand the conclusion
Al-Razi states that from these four proofs it is established that efficacy is a third concept distinct from both cause and effect. This is a key metaphysical claim about causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الرابع في بيان أن تأثير الشيء في الشيء، يمتنع أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر وعين الأثر : هو أن كون المؤثر مؤثراً في الأثر ، وكون الأثر أثراً للمؤثر من مقولة المضاف، وأما ذات المؤثر وذات الأثر فليسا كذلك. لأنا إذا قلنا : إن الله تعالى خلق العالم ، فذات المؤثر هي ذات واجب الوجود ، وذات الأثر هو ذات العالم . فثبت بهذه البراهين الأربعة : أنه لو أثر شيء في شيء، لكانت مؤثرية أحدهما في الآخر ليست عين ذات المؤثر، ولا عين ذات الأثر ، بل كانت مفهوماً ثالثاً مغايراً لهما .
The fourth argument in clarifying that the effect (ta'thīr) of a thing upon a thing is impossible to be the very essence of the cause (mu'aththir) and the very essence of the effect (athar) is: that the cause's being a cause (kawn al-mu'aththir mu'aththiran) in the effect, and the effect's being an effect for the cause, belong to the category of relation (al-muḍāf). But the essence of the cause and the essence of the effect are not like that. For when we say: 'Verily God, exalted, created the world,' the essence of the cause is the essence of the Necessary Existent (wājib al-wujūd), and the essence of the effect is the essence of the world. Thus it is established by these four proofs that if one thing affects another, the efficacy (mu'aththariyya) of one in the other is neither the very essence of the cause nor the very essence of the effect, but rather is a third concept (mafhūm thālith) distinct from both.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth proof and the collective conclusion of all four proofs. The fourth proof argues that the cause's being a cause and the effect's being an effect are relational (min muqālati 'l-muḍāf), while the essences themselves are not relational. For example, when God creates the world, His essence is the Necessary Existent, and the world's essence is the world; these essences are not relations. Therefore, efficacy cannot be identical to either essence. The conclusion then states that from these four proofs it is established that efficacy is a third concept distinct from both cause and effect.

Key Terms
المضاف (al-muḍāf)
واجب الوجود (wājib al-wujūd)
مؤثرية (mu'aththariyya)
مفهوم ثالث (mafhūm thālith)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Efficacy is the same as the essence of the cause or the effect.
Correction: Efficacy is a relational third concept distinct from both essences.

Checkpoint

A) Because the essence of the cause is power, and the essence of the effect is weakness.
B) Because the cause's being a cause and the effect's being an effect are relational, while the essences are not.
C) Because the cause and effect are the same thing.
D) Because the cause is eternal and the effect is temporal.

Key Takeaway
Efficacy (mu'aththariyya) is a relational concept distinct from the essences of cause and effect, established by four proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Or do you unconsciously blur the line, imagining God's power as something that 'passes over' into creation? Where in your life do you mentally confuse the Creator with the creation, even in small ways?
?

What practical habit could you adopt to remind yourself daily that your very being is a relational reality sustained by Another?

Why Efficacy Cannot Be a Negative Concept
Al-Razi proves that efficacy cannot be a negative concept, giving two reasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that efficacy (mu'aththariyya) must be a positive concept, not a mere negation or absence.

Core Idea
Efficacy is positive because its negation is purely negative.

Al-Razi argues against the claim that efficacy is a negative concept. He uses the logical relationship of contradictories to show that if 'not affecting' is pure negation, then 'affecting' must be a positive reality. This lesson walks through the two reasons he gives to disprove that efficacy could be a negative concept.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation to grasp Al-Razi's argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the logical framework
Notice that Al-Razi first divides the distinct concept into negative or positive, then proves it cannot be negative.
The two reasons use contradictory logic and self-contradiction.
3
Analyze the first reason
The first reason uses the relationship of contradictories: if 'not affecting' is purely negative, then 'affecting' must be positive.
This is a key logical principle in kalam.
4
Analyze the second reason
The second reason shows that calling efficacy non-existential (ʿadamī) would simply negate it, which is absurd.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: Why does this matter for causality and theology? Efficacy is real and positive, not a mere absence.
This reinforces the reality of causal relationships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يقال المفهوم من المؤثرية مفهوم ثالث مغاير لذات المؤثر ولذات الأثر فنقول : هذا أيضاً فاسد ، لأن ذلك المفهوم المغاير إما أن يكون سلبياً أو ثبوتياً ، والقسمان باطلان ، وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون سلبياً لوجهين : الأول : إن قولنا : إن الشيء الفلاني مؤثر في كذا ، نقيض لقولنا : إنه ليس بمؤثر في كذا ، لكن قولنا : إنه ليس مؤثراً في كذا مفهوم سلبي ، لأنا لا نعقل من قولنا للشيء المعين : إنه لم يؤثر في كذا ، ولم يفعل فعلا ، ولم يوجد أثراً إلا النفي المحض والعدم الصرف ، وإذا ثبت أن المفهوم من قولنا : إنه لم يؤثر في كذا هو العدم المحض ، وجب أن يكون المفهوم من قولنا : إنه أثر في كذا أمراً ثابتاً موجوداً . ضرورة أن أحد النقيضين لما كان سلبياً ، وجب كون النقيض الآخر ثبوتياً . الثاني : إنا إذا قلنا المؤثرية مفهوم عدمي ، كان المعنى أنه لا وجود للمؤثرية ، ولا حصول لها ولا معنى لهذا الكلام، إلا التصريح بنفي المؤثرية والأثر
As for the second division—that it is said that the concept of efficacy (mu'aththariyya) is a third concept distinct from the essence of the cause and the essence of the effect—we say: this also is false, because that distinct concept is either negative (salbī) or positive (thubūtī), and both divisions are false. We say that it is impossible for it to be negative for two reasons: The first: our statement 'such-and-such a thing affects so-and-so' is the contradictory (naqīḍ) of our statement 'it does not affect so-and-so.' But our statement 'it does not affect so-and-so' is a negative concept, for we do not understand from our saying of a particular thing 'it did not affect so-and-so, and did not do an act, and did not bring about an effect' except pure negation (nafīy maḥḍ) and absolute non-existence (ʿadam ṣirf). When it is established that the concept of our statement 'it did not affect so-and-so' is pure non-existence, it must be that the concept of our statement 'it affected so-and-so' is a fixed existent (amr thābit mawjūd), necessarily because when one of two contradictories is negative, the other contradictory must be positive. The second: if we say that efficacy is a non-existential concept (ʿadamī), the meaning would be that there is no existence for efficacy and no attainment; and there is no meaning to this speech except the explicit negation of efficacy and [its] effect.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage addresses the second division of the previous conclusion: if efficacy is a third concept, it must be either negative or positive. Al-Razi argues that both are false, but specifically proves that it cannot be negative. He gives two reasons. First, the statement 'X affects Y' is the contradictory of 'X does not affect Y.' The negative statement is purely negative, so its contradictory must be positive. Since one contradictory is negative, the other must be positive, establishing that efficacy is positive. Second, if efficacy were non-existential, then it would mean there is no efficacy—which simply negates it, contradicting the claim that it exists as a concept.

Key Terms
مفهوم سلبي (mafhūm salbī)
مفهوم ثبوتي (mafhūm thubūtī)
نقيض (naqīḍ)
عدم (ʿadam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Efficacy might be a mere absence or negation of causation.
Correction: The argument shows that if efficacy were merely negative, it would contradict the logical relationship of contradictories, and would also be self-defeating. Hence efficacy must be a positive concept.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, why must efficacy be a positive concept?
A) Because the concept of efficacy is more known than its negation.
B) Because the negation of efficacy is purely negative, so its contradictory must be positive.
C) Because all concepts are either negative or positive, and efficacy is not negative.
D) Because efficacy is a relation, which cannot be negative.

Key Takeaway
Efficacy (mu'aththariyya) is a positive concept because its contradictory is pure negation, so it must be a real attribute.

Two Proofs that Effectiveness is a Positive Attribute
Razi presents two reasons against effectiveness being a negative concept.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why effectiveness cannot be a mere negation and must be a positive concept, based on the principle of opposites and the self-refutation of calling it negative.

Core Idea
Effectiveness is positive because its opposite is negative, and calling it negative denies itself.

Some have argued that the concept of effectiveness is merely negative—just the absence of ineffectiveness. But the theologian Fakhr al-Din al-Razi rejects this claim with two clear arguments. This passage presents those arguments, using logical reasoning from the nature of opposites and the self-defeating implication of calling effectiveness a negation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's reasoning come through.
2
Identify the two reasons
Razi gives two reasons why effectiveness cannot be a negative concept. Find each and notice how they differ.
The first uses the principle of opposites; the second uses self-refutation.
3
Understand the first argument
Since 'not effective' is a negative concept, its opposite 'effective' must be positive. This follows from the logical rule that one of two opposites must be positive.
Opposites cannot both be negative.
4
Understand the second argument
If effectiveness were a mere negation, then saying 'effectiveness' would simply mean denying effectiveness and effect—a contradiction. Thus, it must be a positive reality.
This argument shows the position is self-defeating.
5
Reflect on the significance
Why does this matter? Establishing effectiveness as a positive concept is crucial for defending causal powers as real attributes in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنقول : هذا أيضاً فاسد ، لأن ذلك المفهوم المغاير إما أن يكون سلبياً أو ثبوتياً ، والقسمان باطلان ، وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون سلبياً لوجهين : الأول : إن قولنا : إن الشيء الفلاني مؤثر في كذا ، نقيض لقولنا : إنه ليس بمؤثر في كذا ، لكن قولنا : إنه ليس مؤثراً في كذا مفهوم سلبي ، لأنا لا نعقل من قولنا للشيء المعين : إنه لم يؤثر في كذا ، ولم يفعل فعلا ، ولم يوجد أثراً إلا النفي المحض والعدم الصرف ، وإذا ثبت أن المفهوم من قولنا : إنه لم يؤثر في كذا هو العدم المحض ، وجب أن يكون المفهوم من قولنا : إنه أثر في كذا أمراً ثابتاً موجوداً . ضرورة أن أحد النقيضين لما كان سلبياً ، وجب كون النقيض الآخر ثبوتياً الثاني : إنا إذا قلنا المؤثرية مفهوم عدمي ، كان المعنى أنه لا وجود للمؤثرية ، ولا حصول لها ولا معنى لهذا الكلام، إلا التصريح بنفي المؤثرية والأثر
We say: This also is corrupt, because that distinct concept is either negative or positive, and both divisions are false. We said: It is impossible for it to be negative for two reasons: First: Our statement 'such a thing is effective in such' is the opposite of our statement 'it is not effective in such', but our statement 'it is not effective in such' is a negative concept, for we do not conceive from our statement of a particular thing 'it did not effect in such, and did not do an act, and did not produce an effect' except pure negation and absolute non-existence. And when it is established that the concept from our statement 'it did not effect in such' is pure non-existence, then it must be that the concept from our statement 'it effected in such' is a positive existent thing, necessarily because when one of the two opposites is negative, the other opposite must be positive. Second: If we say that effectiveness is a non-existent concept, then the meaning is that there is no existence for effectiveness, and no occurrence for it, and there is no meaning for this speech except the explicit denial of effectiveness and effect.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the concept of effectiveness (المؤثرية) is negative (سلبياً). The author presents two arguments. The first argument uses the principle of opposites: the statement 'X is effective in Y' is the opposite of 'X is not effective in Y'. Since 'not effective' is a negative concept, its opposite must be positive. The second argument is that if effectiveness were a mere negation, then saying 'effectiveness' would simply be a denial of effectiveness and effect, which is self-defeating. Thus, effectiveness must be a positive concept.

Misconception: Effectiveness is merely a mental construct with no real existence—it is just the absence of ineffectiveness.
Correction: Effectiveness must be a positive reality because its opposite is a pure negation, and calling it negative would self-destruct.

Checkpoint

B) The principle that one opposite must be positive if the other is negative
C) The principle of infinite regress
D) The principle of correspondence

Key Takeaway
Effectiveness is a positive concept because its negation is a pure negative, and positing it as negative is self-refuting.

Refuting Mental Causality: The Correspondence Argument
Razi argues that effectiveness cannot be merely mental via a correspondence dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that causality cannot be a mere mental concept because the mind's judgment must either correspond to reality or not, and both options lead to the reality of causality.

Core Idea
Causality is real because the mind's judgment about it must match external reality.

Razi presents a powerful refutation of the view that causality is only a mental construct. He uses a logical dilemma: either the mind's judgment that A causes B corresponds to reality or it does not. Both possibilities force us to accept that causation is real, not merely a product of the mind. Let's see how this argument works.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim being refuted
Begin by grasping the position Razi opposes: that effectiveness (al-ta'thir) is a positive concept existing only in the mind, not in external reality. This is the view of those who deny real causality.
This claim is called 'effectiveness as a mental consideration' (i'tibar dhihni).
2
Follow the initial dichotomy
Razi starts with a division: the concept of effectiveness either exists in external reality or it does not (i.e., it is merely mental). He then focuses on the second branch to show its absurdity.
3
Explore the sub-dilemma
If effectiveness is merely mental, then the mind's judgment that 'x is effective on y' either matches external reality or not. Razi examines both possibilities and deduces that each confirms the reality of causation.
This is the core of the argument: correspondence implies real effects; non-correspondence implies falsehood and thus the absurd denial of all causality.
4
Reach the conclusion
Since both options lead to the conclusion that causation is real, the original claim that effectiveness is only mental is refuted. Reflect on why this argument is considered decisive in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوجه الثاني : وهو أن يقال : إن المؤثرية مفهوم ثبوتي مغاير لذات المؤثر ، ولذات الأثر . فنقول : هذا الموجود . إما أن يكون موجوداً في الأعيان ، وإما أن يقال : إنه لا وجود له في الأعيان ، وإنما هو من الاعتبارات الذهنية ، التي لا يكون لها وجود في الأعيان . والقسم الثاني باطل . لأن العقل إذا حكم على الشيء بكونه مؤثراً في شيء آخر. فهذا الحكم الذهني إما أن يكون مطابقاً للأعيان ، وإما أن لا يكون . فإن كان هذا الحكم الذهني مطابقاً لما في الأعيان ، فحينئذ يكون الشيء في الأعيان : أثراً ، ومؤثراً ، وفاعلاً ، ومفعولاً . وحينئذ يبطل قولهم بأن هذه المفهومات : اعتبارات حاصلة في الأذهان ، ولا وجود لها في الأعيان . وإن لم يكن هذا الحكم الذهني مطابقاً للأعيان كان هذا الحكم الذهني كذباً وجهلاً ، وحينئذ لا يكون الشيء في نفس الأمر أثراً ولا مؤثراً ولا فاعلا ولا مفعولاً ، وذلك يوجب القول بنفي التأثير والمؤثر
As for the second aspect, which is that it is said: 'Effectiveness is a positive concept distinct from the essence of the effecter and the essence of the effect.' We say: This existent is either existent in external reality, or it is said that it has no existence in external reality but is rather among mental considerations that have no existence in external reality. The second division is false because when the mind judges a thing to be effective in another thing, this mental judgment either corresponds to external reality or not. If this mental judgment corresponds to what is in external reality, then the thing in external reality is an effect, an effecter, an agent, and an object. Then their statement that these concepts are considerations occurring in the mind with no existence in external reality is invalidated. If this mental judgment does not correspond to external reality, then this mental judgment is false and ignorant, and then the thing in itself is not an effect, nor an effecter, nor an agent, nor an object, and that necessitates the denial of cause and effect.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that effectiveness is a positive concept but exists only in the mind (اعتبار ذهني). The author argues that the mind's judgment that something is effective must either correspond to external reality or not. If it corresponds, then effectiveness must truly exist in external things, contradicting the claim that it is merely mental. If it does not correspond, then the judgment is false, leading to the denial of all causality, which is absurd. Therefore, effectiveness cannot be only mental; it must have real existence.

Key Terms

المطابقة
الأعيان
التأثير
المؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Causality is merely a mental habit or projection; it has no real existence in the external world.
Correction: Razi's argument shows that if causality were only mental, then either the mind's judgment corresponds to reality (making it real) or it does not (leading to the denial of all causation, which is absurd). Therefore, causality cannot be merely mental; it must have real external existence.

Checkpoint

A) Effectiveness is only mental
B) Effectiveness exists in external reality
C) The judgment is false
D) There is no causality

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that causality cannot be merely mental; the mind's judgment about cause and effect must correspond to external reality, proving that causation is real.

Three Arguments Against Effectiveness as a Substance
Razi provides three arguments that effectiveness cannot be a self-subsistent substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational arguments that prevent effectiveness from being considered a self-subsistent substance.

Core Idea
Effectiveness is an attribute of relation, not a standalone substance.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi continues his refutation of the view that effectiveness is a positive concept distinct from the essence, focusing on the claim that it could be a substance. He presents three concise arguments showing why effectiveness cannot be a self-subsistent substance. By examining these arguments, you will see the logical incompatibility between the concept of effectiveness and the category of substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall structure.
Notice the initial division into substance or attribute.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Razi first divides the possible existent thing into substance or attribute. Understand why this dichotomy is exhaustive.
3
Examine the first argument
Analyze why effectiveness cannot be a substance because it is an attribute of the effecter.
Substance cannot be predicated of another.
4
Examine the second argument
Understand the relational nature of cause and effect, which is incompatible with substance.
Relation (مضاف) is not a substance.
5
Examine the third argument
Consider the dilemma: if the supposed substance has no effect it is extraneous; if it has an effect, the same problem recurs.
Leads to infinite regress or irrelevance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القاسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال : كون المؤثر مؤثراً ، أو كون الأثر أثراً : مفهومان مغايران للذات، وهي أمور ثابتة في الأعيان . فنقول : هذا القسم أيضاً باطل ، وذلك لأن ذلك الأمر الوجودي ، إما أن يكون جوهراً قائماً بنفسه ، وإما أن يكون صفة عارضة لذات المؤثر ولذات الأثر ، والأول باطل لوجوه : أحدها : إن المؤثرية صفة لذات المؤثر ، والجوهر القائم بنفسه لا يكون صفة لذات المؤثر . وثانيها : إن المؤثر والأثر من مقولة المضاف، والجوهر القائم بنفسه ليس كذلك . وثالثها : إن هذا الجوهر القائم بنفسه ، إن لم يكن له أثر في ذلك المفعول كان أجنبياً عنه ، وإن كان له فيه أثر فحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور في مؤثرية ذلك الجوهر في ذلك الأثر
As for the second division, which is to say: 'The effecter being an effecter, or the effect being an effect, are two concepts distinct from the essence, and they are things established in external reality.' We say: This division is also false, because that existent thing is either a self-subsistent substance or an accidental attribute of the essence of the effecter and the essence of the effect. The first is false for several reasons: First: Effectiveness is an attribute of the essence of the effecter, and a self-subsistent substance is not an attribute of the essence of the effecter. Second: The effecter and the effect belong to the category of relation, and a self-subsistent substance is not like that. Third: If this self-subsistent substance has no effect in that object, it is extraneous to it; if it does have an effect in it, then the aforementioned division recurs regarding the effectiveness of that substance in that effect.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that effectiveness is a positive concept existing in external reality and that it is a substance (جوهر). The author gives three arguments. First, effectiveness is an attribute (صفة) of the effecter, but a substance cannot be an attribute. Second, effecter and effect are relational (مضاف), but a substance is not relational. Third, if the supposed substance has no effect on the object, it is unrelated; if it does have an effect, then we must examine the effectiveness of that substance in that effect, leading back to the same problem. Therefore, effectiveness cannot be a substance.

Key Terms
الجوهر
الصفة
المضاف
الذات
المؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think effectiveness is a substance-like entity attached to objects.
Correction: Razi shows it is a relational attribute, not a substance.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the arguments against effectiveness being a substance?
A) A substance cannot be an attribute
B) Substance and relation are incompatible categories
C) Substances are eternal and cannot be created
D) A substance without effect is irrelevant, and with effect it leads to regress

Key Takeaway
Effectiveness is a relational attribute, not a substance, as proven by three logical arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Does Razi's argument that cause-effect is merely relational help you see that your reactions are not caused by them, but merely occasions? Refuting Effectiveness as an Attribute Leading to Infinite Regress
Razi argues that if effectiveness were an attribute, it would require another effecter, leading to infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi argues that effectiveness cannot be an attribute, as it leads to an infinite regress that is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
If effectiveness were an attribute, it would need another effecter—and so on forever.

This passage tackles a subtle objection: could 'effectiveness' be a real attribute inherent in the effecter or effect? Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi shows that this leads to an infinite chain of dependencies, which is rationally impossible. The argument is a classic refutation of reifying causal relations as attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim to be refuted
The claim is that effectiveness and effect are attributes subsisting in the effecter and effect respectively. Recognize why someone might think this.
This is the second division of a larger discussion.
2
Follow the chain of dependence
An attribute depends on its subject. The subject is contingent, so it needs an effecter. That effecter's effectiveness would itself be an attribute, leading to another dependence.
This chain is the core of the argument.
3
Why infinite regress is impossible
Razi gives two reasons: first, general proofs against infinite regress; second, even if regress were allowed, the same problem of dependence persists.
Focus on the second reason: the chain never actually explains causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال المؤثرية والأثر صفتان قائمتان بذات المؤثر ، وبذات الأثر . فهذا أيضاً محال لأن الصفة القائمة بالغير مفتقرة إلى الغير والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن لذاته والممكن لذاته لابد له من مؤثر ، فهذه المؤثرية مفتقرة أيضاً إلى مؤثر يؤثر فيه فيكون تأثير ذلك المؤثر في وجود هذه المؤثرية مفهوماً زائداً عليها ، ولزم التسلسل وهو باطل لوجهين : الأول : البراهين الدالة على أن القول بالتسلسل باطل . والثاني : إن على تقدير أن يكون القول بالتسلسل صحيحاً ، فالمحال لازم ههنا أيضاً ، وذلك لأن المعقول من التسلسل أن يستلزم شيء شيئاً
As for the second division, which is to say that effectiveness and effect are two attributes subsisting in the essence of the effecter and the essence of the effect. This is also impossible because an attribute subsisting in another is dependent on the other, and that which is dependent on the other is possible in itself, and that which is possible in itself necessarily needs an effecter. So this effectiveness also is dependent on an effecter that effects it, then the effect of that effecter in the existence of this effectiveness is an additional concept beyond it, and an infinite regress follows, which is false for two reasons: First: The proofs indicating that the claim of infinite regress is false. Second: Even if the claim of infinite regress were correct, the impossibility would still be necessary here, because the intelligible from infinite regress is that one thing necessitates another.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage refutes the possibility that effectiveness is an attribute (صفة) subsisting in the effecter or effect. The author argues that an attribute depends on its subject, and what depends on another is contingent (ممكن), hence needs an effecter. This effecter's effectiveness would itself be another attribute, leading to an infinite chain (تسلسل). This is impossible for two reasons: first, there are proofs against infinite regress; second, even if regress were allowed, the same problem recurs—the chain would never truly explain causality. Thus, effectiveness cannot be an attribute.

Key Terms
الصفة
المفتقر
الممكن
التسلسل
المؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Effectiveness is an inherent attribute that does not need a cause.
Correction: The passage shows that any attribute that depends on another is contingent and thus needs a cause, leading to infinite regress if reified.

Checkpoint
Why does the argument claim that treating effectiveness as an attribute leads to infinite regress?
A) Because attributes are eternal
B) Because each attribute requires another attribute to exist
C) Because attributes are substances
D) Because the mind cannot conceive of attributes

Key Takeaway
Effectiveness cannot be an attribute because it would create an endless chain of causes, which is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you rely on your own abilities, do you treat them as self-sufficient, or do you acknowledge that they are contingent and sustained by the Creator every moment? What would change if you truly internalized that every attribute you possess is dependent on Him?
?
Are there excuses or justifications in your life that form an endless chain—each reason pointing to another reason—so that you never arrive at ultimate accountability before Allah? How does the impossibility of infinite regress call you to stop deferring and submit to the First Cause?
?
This lesson demolishes the idea that a chain of causes can be infinite. Is there an area of your faith or practice where you have been content with an endless 'why' instead of accepting the final 'because Allah says so'? What step can you take today to break that regress?

The First Division: Causality as Mental Judgment
Al-Razi presents and dismisses the mental judgment option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi rejects the idea that causality is merely a mental judgment, as it would lead to the denial of real agency.

Core Idea
Causality cannot be a mere mental illusion—that would make the world unintelligible.

Al-Razi begins his refutation by considering the simplest possibility: that the causal relation is nothing but a mental judgment. He shows why this is unacceptable, because it would reduce all agency to falsehood. This lesson examines that first move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that it presents a conditional statement.
The passage is short but packs a logical argument.
2
Identify the first division
The first division is: causality is a mental judgment. Observe how al-Razi immediately rejects it by pointing out its consequence.
3
Understand the consequence
If causality is mental, then nothing is truly an agent or effect. This leads to a denial of causality itself.
This is a self-defeating position.
4
Reflect on the method
Note that al-Razi uses a reductio: assuming the possibility leads to an absurdity.

يكون هذا الحكم الذهني كذباً وجهلاً، وحينئذ لا يكون الشيء في نفس الأمر أثراً ولا مؤثراً ولا فاعلا ولا مفعولاً، وذلك يوجب القول بنفي التأثير والمؤثر. وأما القاسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: كون المؤثر مؤثراً، أو كون الأثر أثراً: مفهومان مغايران للذات، وهي أمور ثابتة في الأعيان. فنقول: هذا القسم أيضاً باطل، وذلك لأن ذلك الأمر الوجودي، إما أن يكون جوهراً قائماً بنفسه، وإما أن يكون صفة عارضة لذات المؤثر ولذات الأثر، والأول باطل لوجوه: أحدها: إن المؤثرية صفة لذات المؤثر، والجوهر القائم بنفسه لا يكون صفة لذات المؤثر. وثانيها: إن المؤثر والأثر من مقولة المضاف، والجوهر القائم بنفسه ليس كذلك. وثالثها: إن هذا الجوهر القائم بنفسه، إن لم يكن له أثر في ذلك المفعول كان أجنبياً عنه، وإن كان له فيه أثر فحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور في مؤثرية ذلك الجوهر في ذلك الأثر. وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال المؤثرية والأثر صفتان قائمتان بذات المؤثر، وبذات الأثر. فهذا أيضاً محال لأن الصفة القائمة بالغير مفتقرة إلى الغير [والمفتقر إلى الغير] ممكن لذاته والممكن لذاته لابد له من مؤثر، فهذه المؤثرية مفتقرة أيضاً إلى مؤثر يؤثر فيه فيكون تأثير ذلك المؤثر في وجود هذه المؤثرية مفهوماً زائداً عليها، ولزم التسلسل وهو باطل لوجهين: الأول: البراهين الدالة على أن القول بالتسلسل باطل. والثاني: إن على تقدير أن يكون القول بالتسلسل صحيحاً، فالمحال لازم ههنا أيضاً، وذلك لأن المعقول من التسلسل أن يستلزم شيء شيئاً، ويكون الثاني مستلزماً لثالث، ويكون الثالث مستلزماً لرابع، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية. إلا أن هذا المعنى إنما يتقرر عند وجود أمور متلاصقة، يكون كل واحد منها متصلاً بالآخر إلى غير النهاية، إلا أنا إذا قلنا: إن مؤثرية الشيء في الشيء صفة زائدة عليهما، فلا يمكننا أن نشير إلى الشيئين يتصل أحدهما بالآخر إلا ويكون كون أحدهما مستلزماً للآخر أمراً ثالثاً متوسطاً بينهما. وهذا يقتضي أن لا يتصل شيء بشيء آخر البتة، وإذا بطل هذا، بطل القول بالتسلسل، فثبت: أن القول بثبوت التسلسل في هذا المقام يفضى ثبوته إلى عدمه، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوته باطلا. فقد ظهر من جملة ما قررنا: أنه لو أثر شيء في شيء لكان تأثير ذلك المؤثر في الأثر إما أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر أو ذات الأثر، وأما أن يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً لهما، وثبت أن كلا القسمين باطل فاسد، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوت المؤثر والتأثير باطلاً. فإن قال قائل: إن هذا التقسيم الذي ذكرتموه قائم في مواضع قد علم صحتها ووجودها بالضرورة، فوجب أن يكون هذا التقسيم فاسداً، وبيانه من وجهين: الأول: [أن يقال] لو حصلت هذه الدار، وهذا الجدار في هذه الساعة، لكان حصولهما في هذه الساعة، إما أن يكون نفس هذا الشيء، أو نفس هذه الساعة، أو يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً مغايراً، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول [بحصول هذا الشيء في هذه الساعة باطلا، وإنما قلنا: إنه يمتنع أن يكون] حصول هذه الدار وهذا الجدار في هذه الساعة، غير وجود هذه
This mental judgment would be false and ignorance, and then the thing would not in reality be an effect nor an agent nor a doer nor an object, and that necessitates saying the negation of causality and the agent. As for the second division: that it is said: the being of the agent effective, or the being of the effect an effect, are two concepts distinct from the essence, and they are matters established in external entities. So we say: this division is also false, because that existential matter is either a substance subsisting by itself, or an attribute accidental to the essence of the agent and to the essence of the effect. The first is false for reasons: One: that effective-ness is an attribute of the essence of the agent, and the substance subsisting by itself is not an attribute of the essence of the agent. Two: that the agent and effect are from the category of relation, and the substance subsisting by itself is not so. Three: that this substance subsisting by itself, if it has no effect in that object then it is extraneous to it, and if it has an effect in it then the mentioned division returns regarding the effective-ness of that substance in that effect. As for the second division: that it is said effective-ness and effect are two attributes subsisting in the essence of the agent and in the essence of the effect. This is also impossible because the attribute subsisting in another is dependent on another, and what is dependent on another is possible in itself, and the possible in itself necessarily needs an agent. So this effective-ness is also dependent on an agent that affects it, so the effect of that agent in the existence of this effective-ness would be an additional concept beyond it, and an infinite regress follows, which is false for two reasons: First: the proofs indicating that the statement of infinite regress is false. Second: that upon the assumption that the statement of infinite regress is sound, the impossible also follows here, because what is understood from infinite regress is that one thing entails another, and the second entails a third, and the third entails a fourth, and so on to infinity. But this meaning is only established when there exist contiguous things, each one of them connected to the other to infinity, but if we say: that the effective-ness of a thing in a thing is an attribute additional to both, then we cannot point to two things being connected one to the other except that the being of one entailing the other is a third intermediary between them. And this necessitates that nothing is ever connected to another thing, and if this is false, then the statement of infinite regress is false. So it is established: that the statement of the existence of infinite regress in this case leads by its existence to its non-existence, so necessarily the statement of its existence is false. So it has become clear from the totality of what we have established: that if something affects something, then the effect of that agent in the effect is either identical to the essence of the agent or the essence of the effect, or is a third concept for them both, and it has been established that both divisions are false and corrupt, so necessarily the statement of the existence of the agent and causality is false. So if someone says: this division you have mentioned holds in cases whose soundness and existence are known necessarily, so this division must be false. Its clarification is from two aspects: First: [it is said] if this house and this wall exist at this hour, then their existence at this hour would be either the same as the thing, or the same as the hour, or a third distinct concept. The three divisions are false, so the statement [of the existence of this thing at this hour is false, but we say: it is impossible that] the existence of this house and this wall at this hour is other than the existence of this... [text breaks]
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an extended refutation of the reality of causal efficacy (al-ta'thir wa al-mu'aththir). The author (Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) uses a division and reductio argument. He first considers the mental judgment of causality: if the causal relation were merely a mental concept, then things would not be truly effective or affected, leading to a denial of causation itself. This first division is thus rejected. The second division considers causality as a real attribute distinct from essences. He then splits this into two possibilities: the attribute is either a substance (jawhar) or an accident (sifa). The substance option is false for three reasons: (1) effectiveness is an attribute of the agent's essence, but a substance is not an attribute; (2) agent and effect are relative (idafa), but a substance is not; (3) if the substance has no effect on the object it is extraneous, and if it has an effect, the same division recurs. The accident option is also impossible: an accident depends on a subject, and what depends on another is possible in itself, requiring an agent. This leads to an infinite regress (tasalsul) which is false. Moreover, even if regress were possible, effective-ness as an added attribute would prevent the required contiguity between agent and effect, making connection impossible. Therefore both divisions are false, so the belief in causality is false. An objector then raises a counterexample: the division applies to known cases like a house existing at a time, which must be either the house, the time, or a third concept, all of which are impossible, so the division itself must be false. The passage breaks off mid-response to this objection.

التأثير
المؤثر
الأثر
الحكم الذهني

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the consequence if causality is merely a mental judgment?
A) It affirms causality as real.
B) It leads to the denial of causality.
C) It proves that God is the only agent.
D) It is neutral.

Key Takeaway
The first division shows that reducing causality to a mental judgment is self-defeating because it would make all causal terms false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you treated every cause in your life as an illusion, would you still pray with conviction that Allah hears and responds? This lesson argues that denying real causality destroys the reality of divine action. Do you live as if Allah truly causes things in your life, or do you reduce His actions to mere mental concepts?
?
Think of a time when you felt your efforts were meaningless. Did that feeling arise because you doubted that your actions produce real effects? This passage exposes that such doubt leads to denying that you are a real agent created by the Real Agent. How does affirming real causality restore meaning to your daily struggles?
?
If you could no longer say 'Allah caused this' with certainty, what would remain of your faith? This lesson shows that rejecting real causality forces you to deny the very concept of an agent. Do you truly believe that Allah is the agent behind every event, or do you hold a mental judgment that fails to impact your trust?

Causality and Created Things

The Second Division: Substance Option Refuted
Al-Razi refutes the substance option with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's three arguments against the possibility that causal efficacy is a self-subsistent substance.

Core Idea
A substance cannot serve as a causal attribute; it would be neither an attribute nor a relation.

Al-Razi now considers the second division: that causality is a real attribute distinct from the essences of cause and effect. He first examines the possibility that this attribute is a substance, and gives three reasons why it is impossible. This lesson walks through those reasons.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the substance option
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three reasons introduced by 'one', 'two', 'three'.
These are enumerated, so follow the numbers.
2
Identify the first reason
Effectiveness is an attribute of the agent's essence, but a substance is not an attribute.
3
Identify the second reason
The cause-effect relationship belongs to the category of relation (idafa), but a substance is not relational.
4
Identify the third reason
If the substance has no effect, it is extraneous; if it does, the same division applies, leading to regress.
5
Synthesize
Together, these reasons show the substance option is impossible.

Commentary
This passage is an extended refutation of the reality of causal efficacy (al-ta'thir wa al-mu'aththir). The author (Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) uses a division and reductio argument. He first considers the mental judgment of causality: if the causal relation were merely a mental concept, then things would not be truly effective or affected, leading to a denial of causation itself. This first division is thus rejected. The second division considers causality as a real attribute distinct from essences. He then splits this into two possibilities: the attribute is either a substance (jawhar) or an accident (sifa). The substance option is false for three reasons: (1) effectiveness is an attribute of the agent's essence, but a substance is not an attribute; (2) agent and effect are relative (idafa), but a substance is not; (3) if the substance has no effect on the object it is extraneous, and if it has an effect, the same division recurs. The accident option is also impossible: an accident depends on a subject, and what depends on another is possible in itself, requiring an agent. This leads to an infinite regress (tasalsul) which is false. Moreover, even if regress were possible, effective-ness as an added attribute would prevent the required contiguity between agent and effect, making connection impossible. Therefore both divisions are false, so the belief in causality is false. An objector then raises a counterexample: the division applies to known cases like a house existing at a time, which must be either the house, the time, or a third concept, all of which are impossible, so the division itself must be false. The passage breaks off mid-response to this objection.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if causality is real, it must be a separate substance.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that a substance cannot serve as a causal attribute because it is not an attribute, it is not relational, and it leads to regress.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of al-Razi's reasons against the substance option?
A) A substance cannot be an attribute.
B) Cause and effect are relational, but a substance is not.
C) The substance would have to be created by God.
D) If the substance has an effect, the division recurs.

Key Takeaway
The substance option for causal efficacy is impossible because a substance cannot be an attribute, is not relational, and leads to a regress of divisions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often attribute the good in your life to your own efforts or the means you use. But Al-Razi argues that a mere substance cannot be a true cause. Will you today consciously trace every blessing back to its true source—Allah—and thank Him alone, even if the means seem apparent?
?
When you fail or fall short, do you blame the 'substances' around you—people, circumstances, your own abilities—rather than your relationship with Allah? How can you use this lesson to abandon such misattribution and turn back to Allah in repentance and reliance?
?
Al-Razi warns that if a supposed cause has no real effect, it is extraneous. Examine your acts of worship: Are they mere routines (substances) without heartfelt connection? What will you change today to ensure your deeds are not extraneous but truly effective through Allah's acceptance?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate

The Accident Option and Infinite Regress
Al-Razi refutes the accident option and concludes the refutation of causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's refutation of causality as an accident, including his two arguments against infinite regress.

Core Idea
Causality as an accident leads to infinite regress and makes causal connection impossible.

Now al-Razi examines the second possibility under the real attribute division: that causality is an accident (attribute) inhering in the cause and effect. He shows this leads to an infinite regress, and even if regress were allowed, it would preclude any genuine connection. This lesson unpacks that powerful argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the accident option argument
Read the passage fully. Note the two parts: first, the regress argument; second, the connection argument.
2
Understand the regress argument
An accident depends on a subject, so the causal attribute is contingent and needs its own agent, leading to regress.
This is a standard kalam argument: the possible needs a cause.
3
Understand the second argument
Even if regress were possible, an additional attribute would prevent direct contiguity between cause and effect.
This is a deeper point about the nature of connection.
4
See the conclusion
Both sub-options under the real attribute division are false, so causality itself is denied.

Source Text

يكون هذا الحكم الذهني كذباً وجهلاً، وحينئذ لا يكون الشيء في نفس الأمر أثراً ولا مؤثراً ولا فاعلا ولا مفعولاً، وذلك يوجب القول بنفي التأثير والمؤثر. وأما القاسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال: كون المؤثر مؤثراً، أو كون الأثر أثراً: مفهومان مغايران للذات، وهي أمور ثابتة في الأعيان. فنقول: هذا القسم أيضاً باطل، وذلك لأن ذلك الأمر الوجودي، إما أن يكون جوهراً قائماً بنفسه، وإما أن يكون صفة عارضة لذات المؤثر ولذات الأثر، والأول باطل لوجوه: أحدها: إن المؤثرية صفة لذات المؤثر، والجوهر القائم بنفسه لا يكون صفة لذات المؤثر. وثانيها: إن المؤثر والأثر من مقولة المضاف، والجوهر القائم بنفسه ليس كذلك. وثالثها: إن هذا الجوهر القائم بنفسه، إن لم يكن له أثر في ذلك المفعول كان أجنبياً عنه، وإن كان له فيه أثر فحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور في مؤثرية ذلك الجوهر في ذلك الأثر. وأما القسم الثاني: وهو أن يقال المؤثرية والأثر صفتان قائمتان بذات المؤثر، وبذات الأثر. فهذا أيضاً محال لأن الصفة القائمة بالغير مفتقرة إلى الغير [والمفتقر إلى الغير] ممكن لذاته والممكن لذاته لابد له من مؤثر، فهذه المؤثرية مفتقرة أيضاً إلى مؤثر يؤثر فيه فيكون تأثير ذلك المؤثر في وجود هذه المؤثرية مفهوماً زائداً عليها، ولزم التسلسل وهو باطل لوجهين: الأول: البراهين الدالة على أن القول بالتسلسل باطل. والثاني: إن على تقدير أن يكون القول بالتسلسل صحيحاً، فالمحال لازم ههنا أيضاً، وذلك لأن المعقول من التسلسل أن يستلزم شيء شيئاً، ويكون الثاني مستلزماً لثالث، ويكون الثالث مستلزماً لرابع، وهكذا إلى غير النهاية. إلا أن هذا المعنى إنما يتقرر عند وجود أمور متلاصقة، يكون كل واحد منها متصلاً بالآخر إلى غير النهاية، إلا أنا إذا قلنا: إن مؤثرية الشيء في الشيء صفة زائدة عليهما، فلا يمكننا أن نشير إلى الشيئين يتصل أحدهما بالآخر إلا ويكون كون أحدهما مستلزماً للآخر أمراً ثالثاً متوسطاً بينهما. وهذا يقتضي أن لا يتصل شيء بشيء آخر البتة، وإذا بطل هذا، بطل القول بالتسلسل، فثبت: أن القول بثبوت التسلسل في هذا المقام يفضى ثبوته إلى عدمه، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوته باطلا. فقد ظهر من جملة ما قررنا: أنه لو أثر شيء في شيء لكان تأثير ذلك المؤثر في الأثر إما أن يكون عين ذات المؤثر أو ذات الأثر، وأما أن يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً لهما، وثبت أن كلا القسمين باطل فاسد، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوت المؤثر والتأثير باطلاً. فإن قال قائل: إن هذا التقسيم الذي ذكرتموه قائم في مواضع قد علم صحتها ووجودها بالضرورة، فوجب أن يكون هذا التقسيم فاسداً، وبيانه من وجهين: الأول: [أن يقال] لو حصلت هذه الدار، وهذا الجدار في هذه الساعة، لكان حصولهما في هذه الساعة، إما أن يكون نفس هذا الشيء، أو نفس هذه الساعة، أو يكون مفهوماً ثالثاً مغايراً، والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة، فكان القول [بحصول هذا الشيء في هذه الساعة باطلا، وإنما قلنا: إنه يمتنع أن يكون] حصول هذه الدار وهذا الجدار في هذه الساعة، غير وجود هذه
This mental judgment would be false and ignorance, and then the thing would not in reality be an effect nor an agent nor a doer nor an object, and that necessitates saying the negation of causality and the agent. As for the second division: that it is said: the being of the agent effective, or the being of the effect an effect, are two concepts distinct from the essence, and they are matters established in external entities. So we say: this division is also false, because that existential matter is either a substance subsisting by itself, or an attribute accidental to the essence of the agent and to the essence of the effect. The first is false for reasons: One: that effective-ness is an attribute of the essence of the agent, and the substance subsisting by itself is not an attribute of the essence of the agent. Two: that the agent and effect are from the category of relation, and the substance subsisting by itself is not so. Three: that this substance subsisting by itself, if it has no effect in that object then it is extraneous to it, and if it has an effect in it then the mentioned division returns regarding the effective-ness of that substance in that effect. As for the second division: that it is said effective-ness and effect are two attributes subsisting in the essence of the agent and in the essence of the effect. This is also impossible because the attribute subsisting in another is dependent on another, and what is dependent on another is possible in itself, and the possible in itself necessarily needs an agent. So this effective-ness is also dependent on an agent that affects it, so the effect of that agent in the existence of this effective-ness would be an additional concept beyond it, and an infinite regress follows, which is false for two reasons: First: the proofs indicating that the statement of infinite regress is false. Second: that upon the assumption that the statement of infinite regress is sound, the impossible also follows here, because what is understood from infinite regress is that one thing entails another, and the second entails a third, and the third entails a fourth, and so on to infinity. But this meaning is only established when there exist contiguous things, each one of them connected to the other to infinity, but if we say: that the effective-ness of a thing in a thing is an attribute additional to both, then we cannot point to two things being connected one to the other except that the being of one entailing the other is a third intermediary between them. And this necessitates that nothing is ever connected to another thing, and if this is false, then the statement of infinite regress is false. So it is established: that the statement of the existence of infinite regress in this case leads by its existence to its non-existence, so necessarily the statement of its existence is false. So it has become clear from the totality of what we have established: that if something affects something, then the effect of that agent in the effect is either identical to the essence of the agent or the essence of the effect, or is a third concept for them both, and it has been established that both divisions are false and corrupt, so necessarily the statement of the existence of the agent and causality is false. So if someone says: this division you have mentioned holds in cases whose soundness and existence are known necessarily, so this division must be false. Its clarification is from two aspects: First: [it is said] if this house and this wall exist at this hour, then their existence at this hour would be either the same as the thing, or the same as the hour, or a third distinct concept. The three divisions are false, so the statement [of the existence of this thing at this hour is false, but we say: it is impossible that] the existence of this house and this wall at this hour is other than the existence of this... [text breaks]
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an extended refutation of the reality of causal efficacy (al-ta'thir wa al-mu'aththir). The author (Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) uses a division and reductio argument. He first considers the mental judgment of causality: if the causal relation were merely a mental concept, then things would not be truly effective or affected, leading to a denial of causation itself. This first division is thus rejected. The second division considers causality as a real attribute distinct from essences. He then splits this into two possibilities: the attribute is either a substance (jawhar) or an accident (sifa). The substance option is false for three reasons: (1) effectiveness is an attribute of the agent's essence, but a substance is not an attribute; (2) agent and effect are relative (idafa), but a substance is not; (3) if the substance has no effect on the object it is extraneous, and if it has an effect, the same division recurs. The accident option is also impossible: an accident depends on a subject, and what depends on another is possible in itself, requiring an agent. This leads to an infinite regress (tasalsul) which is false. Moreover, even if regress were possible, effective-ness as an added attribute would prevent the required contiguity between agent and effect, making connection impossible. Therefore both divisions are false, so the belief in causality is false. An objector then raises a counterexample: the division applies to known cases like a house existing at a time, which must be either the house, the time, or a third concept, all of which are impossible, so the division itself must be false. The passage breaks off mid-response to this objection.

Key Terms
الصفة
الممكن
التسلسل
المتصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that causality as an accident is plausible because accidents can be added to substances.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that this leads to infinite regress because the accident itself would need a cause, and also prevents direct causal connection.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion drawn at the end of this passage?
A) Causality is real but unknowable.
B) The accident option is false, but the substance option remains.
C) Both divisions (substance and accident) are false, so causality is denied.
D) Infinite regress is possible if there is a first cause.

Key Takeaway
The accident option fails because it leads to infinite regress and, even if regress were allowed, the additional attribute would prevent any direct causal connection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that no created thing has inherent power to cause, then why do you still worry about tomorrow's outcomes as if they depend on your own efforts? Identify one area where you treat a created means as a necessary cause, and commit to reorienting your reliance on Allah alone.
?
When you observe the regularity of the sun rising, do you attribute that to a natural law independent of Allah? How would al-Razi's argument challenge that assumption? What would change in your daily gratitude if you saw each event as directly caused by Allah?
?
Al-Razi’s proof shows that causality even as an attribute leads to absurdity. Have you ever placed your trust in a 'cause'—like a job, a person, or your own abilities—as if it carried necessity? In what specific situation will you actively remind yourself that Allah alone is the true agent?
